The Anglo-French Conference Begins: Discussing the European Situation and the Navy; Britain Does Not Join the New European Alliance; Only Willing to Uphold the Locarno Treaty 47

(London) Authorities from Britain and France began negotiations today in London, which will have a significant impact on the future situation. Observers believe that the initial meeting between the two countries will develop into a discussion of naval armaments, as British First Lord of the Admiralty Monsell and French Minister of Marine Piétri each attended the meeting with their respective secretaries. Both sides are keeping the content of the meeting strictly confidential, but a communiqué may be issued later. The French delegation, consisting of Foreign Minister Barthou, Minister of Marine Piétri, Secretary-General of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Léger, and Director of the League of Nations Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Massigli, went to the British Foreign Office at 10:30 this morning and began the meeting with British Foreign Secretary Simon, Lord Privy Seal Eden, Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs Stanhope, and Bolton. The French delegation arrived in London at 11:18 last night. Foreign Secretary Simon led a number of British officials and personnel from the French Embassy in Britain to the station to welcome them. (9th, National Telegram)

(London) The Anglo-French talks began today, without any predetermined agenda, with the intention of allowing Barthou to freely express his views. The British are particularly concerned about the issue of a "Eastern Locarno" treaty. Regarding the naval issue, the French representatives will only have a preliminary exchange of views during their stay in Britain. Minister of Marine Piétri may extend his stay by twenty-four hours, but he will likely return to France with Barthou on Tuesday. (9th, Havas Dispatch)

(London) French Foreign Minister Barthou, along with Minister of Marine Piétri, is stationed here. The result of Barthou's visit will not be recorded in any official documents. Britain will likely do no more than reiterate its loyalty to the obligations of the Locarno Treaty and its sympathy for France's attitude. Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain spoke in Birmingham and denied that Britain intended to form an alliance with France, saying that rumors that Barthou's visit was related to a secret plan to have Britain join a new European alliance were completely unbelievable. "We are not joining any new alliances and do not want to relax our efforts towards pacifism." (9th, Reuters Dispatch)

(London) French Foreign Minister Barthou, in response to inquiries from representatives of the British press, declared, "The purpose of this consultation between the two great democratic governments is to strive to achieve peace." Beyond this, Barthou declined to elaborate on the content of the talks. The Anglo-French talks will continue at 3:00 p.m. (9th, Havas Dispatch)

Unease in the Hearts of Germans: Most Stormtroopers Do Not Return to Their Units; Extreme Killings Cause Hatred in People's Hearts 48

(Berlin) On the surface, Germany appears calm, but undercurrents of instability continue to make Germans uneasy. The main reason is that 75% of the three million armed stormtroopers will not return to their units after their leave expires this month. The extreme killings in the past week have also caused hatred in the hearts of people across the country, providing material for opposition propaganda. There are many left-leaning dissidents among the disgruntled stormtroopers. The government currently has 100,000 national defense soldiers, Göring's special forces of 12,000 men, and Hitler's Brownshirts of 20,000 men. (7th, China Press Special Dispatch)

⊙Basel The directors of the Bank for International Settlements held a preliminary meeting today. It is generally believed that Germany's announcement of a six-month suspension of debt repayments is the main issue to be discussed at the meeting. It is also rumored that the meeting will discuss the elimination of obstacles to the formal participation of the United States in the bank's business. The meeting is being held in strict secrecy. Participants include Harrison, President of the Federal Reserve Bank of New York, and Vice President Yarborough, Norman, Governor of the Bank of England, and Schacht, President of the Deutsche Bank. (8th, Reuters Dispatch)

(New York) The American Foreign Bondholders Protective Council published a publication containing an article by its chairman, Winckler, on Germany's suspension of foreign debt principal and interest payments, stating, "Germany's situation is becoming increasingly chaotic. If countries do not take appropriate measures to protect the interests of their people and to prevent Germany from becoming a permanent danger to Europe and the world, this kind of peaceful intervention will not cause resistance on the part of the majority of the German people. The situation is the same as in 1923, when France and its allies occupied the Ruhr because Germany refused to pay reparations. French purchases of the Dawes and Young loans account for the majority. If Germany suspends payments on the two types of loans, France will take the opportunity to demand that Germany respect the original contracts. If Germany refuses or is unable to respect them, France will take action to protect the interests of the French people." Winckler went on to analyze and explain how precarious Germany's finances, economy, and political situation are under Hitler's rule, saying, "Hitler and his party said that after the party took power, Germany would become a paradise. In fact, what Hitler said was a decorative phrase and did not correspond to reality at all. Looking at Germany's relations with its neighbors, they are becoming increasingly difficult. Germany and Poland were originally enemy countries. Although they have now signed a treaty, Germany has made all kinds of concessions to Poland, while Poland has given nothing to Germany. Once something happens, Germany will certainly not be able to get help from its eastern neighbor. Italy's Mussolini cannot help Germany. Anyone who knows a little about Mussolini and his policies can say this. Hitler's meeting with Mussolini in Venice in mid-June was no different than returning empty-handed. As for countries such as Romania and Greece, they cannot be regarded as friends of Germany. Unless Germany cancels its demands to amend existing treaties, these countries will not be able to join hands with Germany. Hitler has spent countless propaganda expenses abroad to make foreigners express sympathy for Germany's new politics. However, this kind of money is no different than throwing it into a bottomless pit. In terms of sentiment, Austria should be a friend and ally of Germany, but now it has become an irreconcilable enemy. Therefore, Germany is currently isolated internationally, far more so than it was twenty years ago." Winckler believes that what Hitler and his party are doing is a disastrous policy that will not stop until it is subverted. (8th, Havas Dispatch)

Changes in the German Situation: Hitler's Confidante Issues a Declaration 49

(Berlin) All national concentration camps will henceforth be under the jurisdiction of Himmler, the commander of the secret police and the Nazi SS, as Himmler made great efforts in quelling the previous incident. The stormtrooper guards at the Oranienburg concentration camp have now been withdrawn and replaced by Hitler's hand-picked SS. It is said that this matter has been brewing for a long time and is now being realized. (9th, National Telegram)

(Berlin) Hess, the Minister Without Portfolio in charge of Nazi Party affairs on behalf of Hitler, recently issued a declaration regarding the recent incident, stating, "The execution of a small number of traitors was necessary. Otherwise, thousands of outstanding Germans would have died an unnatural death, and even women and children would have been affected. As for the stormtroopers, they have nothing to do with this rebellion. The traitors were only a few senior leaders and reactionary intellectuals. In addition, the stormtroopers have always been loyal to Hitler. I once gave a speech in Cologne, asking everyone to pay attention to those who advocate a second revolution and not be fooled by them. These people have now been executed. If anyone still intends to slander the stormtroopers, I will issue the same warning to these people. Since the execution of the criminals, our relationship with the stormtroopers has returned to what it was before, and in this campaign, Hitler personally went to the stormtroopers to eliminate the traitors, proving that Hitler has the ability to lead the entire country alone. Hitler and the German people have a pure ideal belief. The German people all know that under Hitler's leadership, they will lead their wives and children to fight for this ideal belief." Hess continued to describe the general situation of the June 30 incident and then strongly asserted that the use of severe measures to eliminate the chaos was appropriate, saying that this was the martial spirit of East Prussia, which only the Nazi Party could represent. "(Hitler saved the country from danger with a strong hand at a critical moment, which we are especially grateful for. And I especially feel that it is necessary to state that all those who have been punished by us have confessed their crimes and have not resisted. I believe that some of them were tempted by a regrettable environment for a while and took the path of crime. But this is a matter of the survival of the German nation. No matter how minor the circumstances of individual crimes are, they should no longer be disputed. In short, in the event of disobedience and rebellion, the method of punishing one to warn a hundred must be used. Although the stormtroopers can never be compared with the army, for the benefit of the people, it is still impossible not to add military discipline and military law to it." Hess then made a plea for peace to the veterans of all countries, especially to the French veterans, saying, "General Hindenburg, the great soldier of East Prussia, is the mainstay of safeguarding peace and saving the motherland. Today, only Germany and Italy are the two countries in the world where veterans control the government. This is definitely not accidental, because these two countries are the most enthusiastic about upholding world peace. And Hitler and Mussolini are both veterans of the Great War. The recent meeting between the two heroes in Venice was seamless. This is also not accidental. As for our neighboring country Poland, since Poland signed a non-aggression treaty with our country, peaceful relations have increased accordingly. However, Pilsudski, who controls the Polish government, is also a veteran of the war. As for the French veterans, there are many who express their support for Hitler's attempt to achieve German-French understanding. In short, all of us veterans do not want to sit idly by and allow a group of incompetent diplomats to trap us in the catastrophe of war and make us suffer. Soldiers of all countries know that the last war should not be the responsibility of the military. If someone asks why I didn't say this before, but only say this today, I dare to answer that I didn't want to say anything a few years ago because I didn't want to make the same remarks as the traitors of Germany. At that time, the traitors of Germany vilified the meritorious front-line soldiers and did not hesitate to sign the Treaty of Versailles. These people even chanted pacifism. I am ashamed of it. Today, I will loudly tell the world that (peaceful Germany) and (pacifist Germany) are very different and should not be confused. You should know that any attempt to let a large army drive into Germany will eventually run into a wall." Hess then spoke specifically to the French veterans, saying, "In the last war, France exhausted all its strength to defend its territory. It would never give up even an inch of land. If someone has war ambitions and intends to inflict on Germany what was inflicted on France in the past, we will shout loudly, 'Dare you attack Germany? Dare you enter German territory?' I know that French veterans will definitely be able to understand our intentions. And this new Germany's ambition will soon be known to the world. The French people know very well how people from all countries defend their territory. We German veterans have to express our respect to the French veterans, because in the last war, the French army shed the most blood for the common interests of the allied countries. Although we often hear speeches made by representatives of the French government that do not fully conform to the spirit of international coordination, we still hope that the French government also has the desire for peace. If the remarks made by representatives of the French government are not consistent with the opinions of the French people and veterans, this is the fault of the parliamentary system." Hess continued to speak, expressing high praise for French Foreign Minister Barthou, with rather abrupt wording, saying that German-French understanding would be beneficial to the people of both countries. Finally, he said, "(Poland, Germany's eastern neighbor, has signed a treaty with us to guarantee peaceful relations between the two neighboring countries. It can be seen that signing a peace treaty is more secure than expanding military strength. This will soon be understood by other neighboring countries." (8th, Havas Dispatch)

Germany Suspends Debt Payments: Attempting to Accumulate Funds for War; Commentary by the Russian Pravda 50

(Moscow) The Soviet Russian Communist Party's organ, Pravda, reported that Germany has suspended debt payments in the hope of using its gold reserves for war preparations. The newspaper went on to say that Germany's increase in military spending by 33% has caused foreign countries to be alarmed, but this is only the beginning. The newspaper considered the most noteworthy aspect to be Germany's commercial figures, stating that while Germany's manufactured goods exports and domestic consumption have declined, imports of certain goods, such as iron, manganese, cotton, and other military raw materials, have increased without decrease. Germany's exports of pig iron and steel in 1933 increased by 31% compared with 1932. Its conclusion is as follows: (1) After the expansion of Germany's heavy industry, domestic consumption or exports have never expanded accordingly, and prices and profits have not fallen. Therefore, this expansion is obviously due to government demand. (2) The increase in imports of certain raw materials, since it has failed to expand domestic and foreign trade, is naturally caused by orders for military industries and the accumulation of military raw materials. (3) 20% of the expansion of German heavy industry and most of the raw materials imported by Germany are used for war preparations. (8th, National Telegram)

Military Buildup Competition: Japan Will Inevitably Lose to the US and Britain - Observations of an American Publisher 52

The Continental Daily reports that American newspaper publisher William Randolph Hearst recently resided at the Cardiff Villa in Wales, England. Representatives from the local Western Mail and South Wales News visited him to inquire about his opinions on President Roosevelt's naval plan and the current state of the Japanese navy. Hearst replied that he particularly supports President Roosevelt's view that, for the sake of world civilization and peace, disarmament should be prioritized. However, if the world engages in an arms race, the United States will resolutely not lag behind and fall into a dangerous situation. Hearst also said that the Japanese claim they want to build a massive navy, but their financial resources cannot sustain it. He believes that no civilized country should truly spend money that could be used for peaceful development on military buildup. However, the United States will not allow Japan's aggressive military power to exceed its own defensive military power. The United States has always opposed war, so they are willing to generously sacrifice money and lives to protect their coast from war and the horrors of invasion. If there is a competition to build warships and airplanes in the future, the British Empire and the United States will surely prevail for three reasons: (1) They have determination and patience, (2) They are rich in money, and (3) Britain's territories and America's commercial shipping routes are vast, and there is a need to maintain and protect transportation. Therefore, even in times of peace, they already have many ships and airplanes, which can easily be converted for military use in wartime. Hearst argues that Americans should not overly concern themselves with the situation in the Far East, believing that they should not involve the country in foreign disputes. If China cannot take care of itself, it should bear the consequences. China's failure to adequately defend itself is due to its advocacy of an excessively peaceful policy. It is unfortunate that a nation with 350 million people cannot defend itself against the aggression of a nation with 90 million people. He expresses sympathy for China and regrets China's foolishness, but believes there is no reason for them to get involved in China's disaster.

(Geneva) According to sources from Germany, two German airplanes crashed into Lake Constance today, resulting in the deaths of seven people. The cause is believed to be negligence. Japan's Expansion of Power in North China Will Greatly Impact Europe and the United States - Impressions from Harvard University Professor's Inspection of the Far East - British Tolerance of Japanese Aggression Astonishes People in Shanghai and Peiping 57

(Moscow) Harvard University Professor Hopper, who inspected the situation in China and Japan for three months, passed through here on his way home. He stated that Japan's commercial and political power in North China will greatly impact the Far East trade of Western countries. Professor Hopper also stated his impressions as follows: (1) There is a possibility of a Russo-Japanese war, but it will not break out immediately. (2) Japan is not satisfied with its experience in annexing Korea, and may not repeat this mistake in Manchuria. However, it will try its best to expand its control in Manchuria. (3) British tolerance of Japan's aggressive policy has astonished people in Shanghai and Peiping, because Britain will be the most affected if Japan's aggression succeeds. (9th, National News Agency)

(Moscow) The key to peace or war between the Soviet Union and Japan in the Far East seems to be in the hands of fate. The area along the meandering Heilongjiang River has historically been a famous powder keg. An incident could trigger an explosion at any time. In the past month, Soviet Russian defense troops fired three times at merchant ships of Manchukuo under Japanese protection, allegedly because these merchant ships were suspected of spying on Soviet Russian fortresses along the Heilongjiang River. Both Japan and Russia are actively stockpiling military supplies, and warships and troops are being built and trained. However, influential figures in both countries are still trying their best to maintain peace. Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov has gone to Geneva, hoping to unite the countries that he considers eager to maintain peace. France and the Little Entente may be among the countries that Litvinov considers to be peace-loving. France and the Little Entente are most willing to maintain the status quo created by the Treaty of Versailles, fearing that this status quo will be destroyed by war. The Soviet Union has long regarded the League of Nations as a tool used by capitalist countries to defend against socialism. Now it has abandoned this accusation and hopes to participate in the Geneva Executive Council. The Soviet Union's change of attitude towards Geneva can also be said to be influenced by Germany and Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations. Soviet Russian politicians have always regarded Germany and Japan as the biggest enemies, and firmly believe that Germany and Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations is aimed at expanding their military power in preparation for future aggression. The Soviet Union believes that other countries in the League of Nations, with a few exceptions, are all friends of peace. If the Soviet Union unites with the member states of the League of Nations, it can strengthen its resistance to Germany and Japan. The Soviet Union now wants to use war to stop war and eliminate past concerns in Geneva. No one in Moscow believes that Litvinov hopes that France and other League of Nations member states will send troops to help if war breaks out between Russia and Japan. However, it is believed that the coordination between the Soviet Union and the League of Nations member states, especially with France, will reduce the fear of attack from the west and increase the courage to attack from the east if war breaks out between Russia and Japan in the East. Soviet Russian politicians now believe that Germany and Japan have a tacit understanding in spirit and are sacrificing the Soviet Union to benefit themselves. They also believe that if the Soviet Union goes to war with either Germany or Japan, the other country will definitely take the opportunity to attack the Soviet Union. This kind of thinking can be seen in Moscow newspapers at any time. The main factors influencing peace or war in the Far East are as follows: (1) Disputes over the Chinese Eastern Railway, which is jointly owned by China and the Soviet Union. Japan is trying to seize the railway in the name of Manchukuo. (2) The two countries are arguing about the price that Japan should pay for fishing in Soviet Russian territorial waters. (3) The Soviet Union deeply believes that Japan has ambitions to occupy the Primorsky Krai. Most observers do not believe that the first two factors will lead to war between the two countries. Most people familiar with the situation in the East deeply believe that the Soviet Union would rather lose the Chinese Eastern Railway than resolve the railway rights issue by force. Although the fisheries dispute is serious, it will also be resolved through tolerant negotiations. However, last year, Soviet Russian politicians repeatedly declared that they would never lose an inch of national territory. Therefore, Japan's ambition to invade and occupy the Primorsky Krai is most likely to lead to war. In the future, if ships from Manchukuo or Japan approach the Soviet Russian coast, or if conflicts occur between the defense troops of the two countries at night, it is easy to cause this kind of misunderstanding and cause war. (9th, National News Agency)

(Tokyo) The Okada Cabinet's national defense and diplomatic policies will follow the policies of the previous cabinet. (9th, Japan United Press)

It also appointed Itō Shin as the new Finance Minister, recommended by former Finance Minister Takahashi. This is undoubtedly intended to follow the Saito Cabinet's national defense, diplomatic, and financial policies to deal with the crisis of 1935. After the policy is decided at the five-minister conference and passed by the cabinet, it will be clearly announced at home and abroad. In addition to these fundamental policies, the new cabinet's policies are: (1) Just and fair politics, (2) Rectification of discipline, (3) Stabilization of national life, (4) Rural countermeasures, and reform of the electoral system. The Saito Cabinet fell due to disciplinary problems. The Okada Cabinet paid special attention to this when deciding on cabinet members, consulting the opinion of the new Minister of Justice Ohara. Implementing just and fair politics is the fundamental basis for stabilizing people's hearts, and stabilizing national life is the fundamental meaning of guiding thought. The rice and silkworm cocoon problems of rural countermeasures are also awaiting resolution. As for reforming the electoral system, it is one of the important missions of the Okada Cabinet. For this cabinet issue, Okada specially appointed former Minister of Agriculture Gotō as Minister of Home Affairs, rejecting the political parties' scramble for this position. Okada has seen through that the next parliament will be dissolved and is determined to use a neutral Minister of Home Affairs to implement fair elections. (9th, Japan United Press)

(Tokyo) The policies and ambitions of each cabinet member of the Okada Cabinet, which has a new lineup to deal with the current crisis, are generally as follows: Minister of Home Affairs Gotō said that he will tighten finances, appoint personnel based on their talents, and follow the policies of former Minister of Home Affairs Yamamoto for relief work. Minister of Justice Ohara said that according to Prime Minister Okada's wishes, he will thoroughly rectify discipline and eliminate the people's anxieties. The Ōkura incident will also be handled in this spirit. For elections, he will definitely follow the new election law and strive to eliminate abuses. Minister of Commerce and Industry Machida said that the historical opposition between the Ministry of Agriculture and the Ministry of Commerce and Industry is not good for the country. He will definitely strive to harmonize the opposition between small and medium-sized enterprises and industrial associations, and the industrial rationalization problem. He will review the policies of his predecessor and establish concrete measures from a broad perspective. Minister of Communications Tokuda said that he is a complete layman in communications and will seek guidance from all sectors in the future. He will first strive to dedicate himself to social policy measures for current employees. (9th, Domei News Agency)

(Tokyo) Secretary General Takayama Sanpei of the Colonial Affairs Ministry met with Prime Minister Okada yesterday and then attended a meeting of the Colonial Affairs Ministry to report the government's policy, saying that the government believes that the military and foreign ministries have conditions attached, and there are no suitable successors for the time being, so the prime minister will temporarily serve concurrently. The rumor that the Colonial Affairs Ministry will be abolished is completely unfounded. If there are changes in the future, it may be expanded. Also, the heads of colonial territories and the South Manchuria Railway Company will not be changed unless it is their own wish. (9th, Domei News Agency)

The government is now trying to conserve the consumption of drinking water. (8th, Havas)

A Record of Inspection in the Northwest: Special Correspondent of This Newspaper: Ya 74

Seventeen households, no shops, all engaged in agriculture. However, many men and women are addicted to opium. There are more than twenty opium lamps. There is one official opium franchise, paying a monthly franchise fee of thirty-six yuan. The riverbank produces abundant Artemisia grass, which can be used as fertilizer. Those without the capital to cultivate land make a living by collecting Artemisia grass, which sells for 2.5 mao per hundred catties. The farming method is very simple: turn over the soil, spread Artemisia grass underneath, sow seeds, water, and hope for a harvest. Cow and horse manure is used as fuel. The spring and autumn grain tax is two dou per mu in total. In summer, they plant green beans and millet; in autumn, wheat and peas, each at three sheng. Poor farmers without capital to plant seeds still have to pay the grain tax, so "fleeing households" are better than "extinct households." One-fifth to one-third of the land is already abandoned.

I heard many folk songs, and have selected a few to record below. One is about: "Opium, one tael is worth a thousand gold coins. Which of the brothers isn't addicted? The sound of the opium pipe being scraped is soft. The half-lit lamp illuminates the long night." The second is: "A square piece of land, planted with mustard seeds for three years. When I pick up my rice bowl, I think of you. My hand trembles, and I can't hold the chopsticks." When this song is sung, it is like weeping and complaining, with a strong sense of "every grain is the result of hard work." It shows that it is difficult to eat, especially difficult for farmers to eat. The third is: "My younger sister has a slender waist and small feet; even dumplings eaten on New Year's Day can't compare." On the Lunar New Year, people eat dumplings, the smaller the better. This song is a metaphor for women's foot binding, which is even smaller than New Year's dumplings. According to information, in Ningxia Province, apart from the gradual liberation of female students in the cities, most people still follow the outdated custom of foot binding, especially Hui women in the countryside. The marriage prospects of ordinary women with unbound feet are often not as good as those with bound feet. Military and political figures in the provincial capital often like to forcibly take female students as concubines, which has caused female students to issue a united call for resistance. Ordinary people also like to keep female servants with natural feet, but when it comes to marrying a wife, they prefer old-fashioned women, saying that they can manage the household and handle trivial matters. This is truly unexpected.

The Strategic Importance of Qingtong Gorge 75

On the 23rd at thirty minutes past early morning, we set off from the dam, twenty li north, to a place called Qingtong Gorge, which controls the vital passage of the Yellow River and is, along with Shizuishan, a natural barrier of Ningxia. It is a strategic location contested in both ancient and modern warfare. There are one hundred and eight circular pagodas there. The Gansu Gazetteer states that it is the Tianmen Fortress. Later generations have added legends and embellishments, saying that the number of pagodas is constantly changing. Every time they are counted, the number is never exactly one hundred and seven or one hundred and nine. It is impossible to get the exact number. A certain military officer led his troops past here and was very skeptical of this claim. He ordered his one hundred and eight followers to each occupy a pagoda and report the number. Suddenly, one person was missing. He added another person and counted, and there were one hundred and nine. This was simply because the person who was missing was snoring and sleeping and then woke up. The reporter does not believe this story. I asked Mr. Du and others to watch over the car, and we continued along the main road, passed the watershed, and went to Guangwuhou to meet. I and Mr. Xu hired a guide and detoured to see it. At first, we walked along the canal and river, sometimes climbing up hills, sometimes taking off our shoes and wading through water. The red cliffs were high, like Western-style buildings. The crows and pigeons lived in the towers, a fitting place for them. When we arrived at our destination, on the riverbank, there was a Dragon King Temple, empty and without anything. When workers dredged the Han Canal mouth in the spring, they could eat and stay here. On a sloping area, white pagodas were densely arranged like dog's teeth. They were divided into twelve levels according to the terrain, the lowest level having nineteen pagodas. Ascending from the lowest to the highest, the number of pagodas gradually decreased until the highest level, which had only one pagoda. Viewed from afar, the overall shape resembled an isosceles triangle. The highest pagoda was about ten feet tall and five arm-spans around. It was conical in shape and contained a clay statue, which, it is said, was the entire body of Mu Guiying. In 1930, Ma Zhongying captured Ningxia and retreated there.

According to this, Men Zhizhong attacked him. Ma won first and then lost. His soldiers suspected that the gods were not protecting them, so they dug out the face of the Mu Guiying clay statue, making it unrecognizable. Moreover, the attire was very similar to that of Guanyin. It is said that the Mu statue is still a question. Behind the pagoda is an ancient temple with many murals of deities. There is a broken pottery item, which seems to be a platform for a deity to sit on. It is engraved with the eight characters "Thousand Buddha Hall, Jiajing Thirty Years." The other pagodas are smaller in shape. When counted one by one, there are only one hundred and six, and the highest pagoda is also included. One of the pagodas has a single base and a double top, which is probably the origin of the suspected number. Also, at the midpoint of the three sides, about ten feet in front, there is a pagoda. This may be the origin of the number one hundred and nine. As for the number "one hundred and eight," it may refer to the number when the main pagoda on the highest level is removed. The terrain is backed by the high ridges of Niutou Mountain, and in front is the Yellow River. The dangerous cliffs and precipices on the opposite bank are impassable even for flying birds. Most of the local people can recite the lines "When you walk to Qingtong Gorge, there are one hundred and eight ancient pagodas. Walk from the big dam to the small dam, the more you walk, the more afraid you become." When asked for details, they are all at a loss for words. Only the strategic importance of the terrain can be discerned.

There is a ferry at the gorge. There are four or five families of villagers on both sides, who make a living by operating the ferry and burning limestone. The river enters the gorge from Zhongwei and flows through the gorge for more than ten li. The river channel is narrow and the water flow is rapid. The mouth of the Han Yan Canal is located at the end of the gorge. The river surface gradually widens, reaching about 300 meters. Stones are piled up at the canal mouth to form a dam, with mud and grass stuffed in between. Its width occupies about one-fifth of the river channel, forcing water into the canal. The width gradually increases, called the "welcoming water dam." The remaining four-fifths of the river channel has leather rafts flowing downstream endlessly. "Leather raft" means that the entire skin of cattle and sheep is peeled off and the limbs and head are tied up and inflated with air, called "huntun." These are tied to a frame of sticks. The smaller ones are called rafts, carrying a thousand catties of goods or six or seven people. The larger ones are called large rafts or leather rafts, capable of carrying 20,000 to 30,000 catties. They float very quickly, traveling 200 to 300 li per day. However, they cannot go upstream. If boats pass through the gorge, there is no way to return. The leather rafts made of cowhide can be loaded with goods. After unloading, the leather can be folded and carried back. If it is a small raft, one person can carry it on their shoulders, which is very convenient. The Yellow River freezes for about four months of the year, and there are shallow obstacles for about three or four months. The period when rafting is smooth is only four or five months out of the year.

In addition, there are so-called "wool rafts" and "wooden rafts," which are also downstream transportation tools in Qinghai, Gansu, and Ningxia. Wool rafts consist of sheepskin bags filled with wool and other items, loaded with fur, water tobacco, and raw opium. Most commonly, they carry wool, hence the name wool raft. Small wool rafts mostly come from Xining and arrive at Lanzhou. As the river widens, several rafts are combined into one large raft, transporting them to various places in Ningsui. The goods and the wood used to connect the leather bags are sold, and the leather bags are carried back to be used again next time. Wooden rafts are made by residents in the upper reaches of the Yellow River, where timber is abundant, who lash wood into rafts and transport a small amount of goods downstream. The size and shape vary. Most of the building materials needed are supplied by the wool and wood rafts from Qinghai and Gansu. After leaving Qingtong Gorge and returning to the main road, we passed through narrow, winding paths. Strange rocks stood on both sides. Walking side by side, our clothes were snagged. A python as thick as a bowl was coiled in the stone path. It seemed to hear our footsteps and immediately retreated into a stone cave, making a croaking sound. The echo resounded in the empty valley, making our hearts grow cold. Climbing over a high ridge, a vast plain suddenly opened up. The yellow canals and green fields resembled those of Ningxian County. We arrived at Guangwu Fortress, having traveled fifty li. The fortress was as large as a city, with only one gate. Most of the fields outside the fortress were uncultivated. When asked, we learned that some people were using hand hoes to till the land, but it was difficult to cultivate even one mu in several days. When asked where their cattle and livestock had gone, they replied, "They have been requisitioned and have not returned." The price of land was previously thirty yuan per mu. Now, due to the heavy taxes and levies after the requisition, they want to sell it for five yuan, but there are still no buyers.

Thirty li to Qukou Fortress, belonging to Zhongning County. The people live in dilapidated earthen houses. However, the Guan Emperor Temple and Guanyin Hall competed to show off their newly renovated and imposing features. The Chinese people pay great respect to the gods and little to the people. This is not unique to one place. Inside the Guan Emperor Temple, there is an attached primary school. The main hall houses a statue of Guan Yu and a plaque with the inscription "Long Live the Emperor, Ten Thousand Years." Five students sit below, reciting Mencius. It is said that when all the students are present, there are more than thirty. Now, because the food for the entire fortress was mostly requisitioned during the war, the people have nothing to eat. Each person leads their children to the outskirts to find wild vegetables. Moreover, it is spring plowing season, and many students have been called back by their parents to help with the farm work. Therefore, the number of students in school is particularly small. Later, along the way, we indeed saw women and children carrying baskets, gathering in the fields or crawling along the paths, vying to find wild vegetables and bean leaves. The miserable scene was unbearable to witness. Fifteen li to Tietong Fortress. The land is mixed with sand and gravel, making it difficult to grow opium. The people cherish it very much. When wheat is planted, each mu yields only three to five dou, with a tax of three sheng, which is only one-eighth of the tax on fertile land in Xiahe and Liangxian counties. Twenty-five li to Zaoyuan. We chose a shop to stay in. That day, we traveled one hundred and twenty li. There were many date stacks in the garden, which were verdant and lovely. Each mu of dates could yield one dan, which was worth seventeen yuan last year. In total, the entire garden weighed 300 catties when wet. In terms of agricultural byproducts, it accounted for a large income. There were about 400 households, with a population of about 1700. Each family lived near their fields. There was a complete primary school and five or six private schools. There were a total of 300 students in public and private schools, accounting for about half of the school-age children. Public schools did not charge tuition fees, and many children from poor families attended them. Private schools charged a regular annual fee of three yuan per person, plus gifts for the four major festivals, as well as miscellaneous fees for ink and paper (2 mao), charcoal (2 mao), incense oil (1 catty), and rice and flour (1 sheng), totaling about six yuan per year. Villagers were superstitious about private schools, praising that "those who are familiar with the Four Books and proficient in the Five Classics do not read textbooks but understand everything." Therefore, they rushed to private schools and did not mind paying high fees. Moreover, many students in public schools had also read the Four Books, so they were older and taller, like middle school students.

When we arrived at Zaoyuan and went to choose a shop, every household was eating dinner. The main food was a basket of wild vegetables, a bowl of noodle soup or mung bean soup, a pot of vinegar, and a plate of salt. Only one in ten people ate steamed buns or porridge. Wild vegetables, often called "bitter bitter vegetables," were the main food among the main foods. Their shape was very similar to poppies and dandelions. Cooked and dipped in vinegar, they still tasted bitter. Young children did not eat it, stopped their chopsticks, and cried. Grain merchants from other counties were often robbed. Local merchants were killed if they were robbed. The bandits wore masks and painted their faces, and were mostly local starving people. It can be seen that there was money to buy a good harvest, but the people had no food. The miserable situation was like this. The calamities of war were even worse than words could describe.

The Water Level of the Yellow River in Shandong Rises Sharply: Water Level Reaches Over 28.19 Meters; Zhang Lianjia Goes to Inspect River Works in the Middle Reaches 76

Jinan Dispatch: The water level of the Yellow River in Shandong is currently in a major flood period. It has continued to rise for days, and it is gradually entering a critical stage. Flood prevention work in all sections is also becoming increasingly tight. Moreover, there have been heavy rains in the upstream area of Shanzhou for days, and the water level has risen sharply. Huge waves and currents are flowing down rapidly. According to a report from Luokou from the Shandong River Affairs Bureau on the 5th, the water level was still 27.48 meters. Today (the 6th), at 6:00 AM, the bureau received another report, stating that from the evening of the 5th to 6:00 AM this morning (the 6th), the river water rose sharply, and the flow was fierce. The water level increased by 7.1 gongcun in just a few hours, reaching 28.19 meters, and is still rising. Fortunately, the condition of the river works in the upper, middle, and lower reaches is still stable, and there have been no major incidents. After receiving the report, Zhang Lianjia, the director of the River Affairs Bureau, feared that the water level would change and cause dangerous works. In addition to ordering the flood prevention sections and county chiefs along the river to step up defenses, he set off by car from Jinan at 2:00 PM today (the 6th) to inspect the middle reaches. After leaving Jinan, Zhang first traveled west along the south bank, passing through the Lijiasi section, Zhuangyangzhuang, Handao Pass, Caojiazhuang, and Zhangzhuang, and arrived at Beidianzi, which is the junction of the first and second main sections of the south bank. After a brief inspection, Zhang crossed the river from Beidianzi to Qihe on the north bank to check the river works. Then, he traveled east along the embankment from Qihe, passing through Wangzhuang, Yue Zhuang, Xi Daokou, Li Jiaan, Zhao Zhuang, Qiu Jiaan, Liu Jiamiao, Wang Jia Kiln, Zhu Heyuan, and Ding Jiakou, and arrived at Luokou. All of the above are located in the third section of the north bank. After completing the inspection, he set off from Luokou and returned to Jinan at 7:30 PM. According to Zhang, the river works in the middle reaches were all in good condition during this trip. Now, because of the heavy rain in the upstream area of Shanzhou, the water level has risen sharply and is flowing downstream. Fortunately, the newly built embankments are not in danger. According to another source, the water level of the Yellow River rose by more than three gongchi this afternoon (the 6th), totaling more than one meter since yesterday, which is more than three Chinese feet. The water level reached 28.3 meters this afternoon and is still rising. However, it is still more than three meters below the highest water level last year. Judging from the current situation, other unexpected incidents are unlikely to occur. Regarding the newly emerged dangerous work in the lower reaches of Lijin Gongjiadong, it has been actively repaired by the river defense personnel and can be considered safe. Fortunately, although the river滩 was washed away by the torrent, it has not yet reached the base of the embankment. Because there is another滩 dam inside the main embankment, which is the dangerous work that was washed away by the water this time. If it is not repaired urgently, it will be very dangerous. It is reported that Pan Jianfen, the chief of the engineering section of the bureau, set off yesterday (the 5th) and has arrived at the work site to supervise the emergency repairs. As for the restoration situation, stones are being placed first, so no matter how large the water flow is, it will not affect the work. Pan now plans to return to Jinan tomorrow (the 7th) because the dangerous work has been completed. In addition, Liang Jinming, the chief of the downstream section, came to Jinan from the flood area a few days ago to meet with Zhang Lianjia, the director of the River Affairs Bureau, to report on the dangerous situation in the downstream area. Liang is scheduled to return to the downstream work section tomorrow (the 7th) after completing his official duties in Jinan to oversee all matters. All work sections along the river have now been carefully defended to avoid negligence. (6th)

Military and Economic Collapse of the Red Bandits: The Military Headquarters Announces the Confession of a Surrendered Bandit from the False Third Division 77

Nanchang Dispatch: Since the Red Bandits were subjected to five encirclement campaigns by the National Army, their military has failed and their economy has fallen into bankruptcy. According to the confession of Ren Wenkui, a document officer from the False Third Division, announced by the Military Headquarters, they are showing signs of total collapse. His confession is as follows: (A. General Situation of the Bandit Area: 1. The people in the bandit area have been subjected to various oppressions by the bandits recently, and there is no way to escape, resulting in many people committing suicide by throwing themselves into wells or hanging themselves. The situation is chilling to witness. 2. The farmers are even more impoverished than before. Each person only receives three or four dan of grain per year and must also bear the burden of public bonds, war expenses, and membership fees. They work hard year-round but cannot make ends meet. Men are forced to become soldiers, and women are oppressed to farm the land. Each person must also pay three sheng of rice per month to send to the front lines. The people dare to be angry but dare not speak out. They wish for the time of their destruction. 3. Workers have no work to do. The number of unemployed has reached over 90%. 4. The bandit area has a national bank that issues banknotes, divided into five denominations: one yuan, five jiao, two jiao, one jiao, and five fen. Five yuan is equivalent to one silver dollar. There are also self-made small silver coins of two hao and one hao. Eighteen hao are equivalent to one silver dollar. Each paper yuan can only buy two or three liang of salt. The high cost of other goods can be imagined. Therefore, the general life is extremely difficult. B. Military Aspect: 1. The main force of the bandits is the 1st, 3rd, 5th, 7th, and 9th Army Corps. Each army corps has three divisions, each division has three regiments, and each regiment has about 500 to 600 people. There are about 300 to 400 guns, and the rest are spearmen. Each soldier has a maximum of seven or eight rows of bullets, and only one-tenth of the guns have bayonets. There are very few hand grenades. 2. The bandits have suffered many failures, and there have been many deaths, injuries, and desertions. Now, the people in the bandit area are all required to join the Red Army. Those under 25 are designated as Young Pioneers, and those over 25 are organized into Model Battalions and Red Guards. Communist Party members are assigned to train them, falsely claiming to protect their homeland, but they are soon sent to the front lines as replacements. There is now talk of expanding the 4th and 12th Army Corps and expanding the Red Army by 50,000. C. Material Aspect: 1. Ammunition is scarce. The bandit leaders once ordered all villages to search for broken copper and scrap iron to prepare for self-manufacturing, but for several months, no one has complied. Recently, only ten dan of scrap iron has been collected in Yudu, which is of no help. The ordnance factory in Yudu can only repair weapons due to a lack of raw materials and cannot manufacture them. 2. Supply is difficult. It is now stipulated that each bandit soldier receives eight liang of rice per day (six liang for dry rice and two liang for porridge). Although a small amount of salt can be transported in from western Fujian, the supply cannot meet the demand, resulting in many soldiers having no salt to eat. 3. Other: I. Bandit soldiers have no clothes to wear, no blankets to cover themselves, and no medicine to treat injuries. Many want to defect. II. Because surveillance is very strict, there is no opportunity to take advantage of. III. Local armed forces such as guerrillas are more likely to defect. IV. Currently, in order to maintain the emergency situation, the bandits are collecting old silver coins from various places to manufacture fake foreign coins and organizing a trade bureau to send people to buy materials from the Central Army and local areas to provide relief. (6th)

Supreme Court: Summary of Annual Meeting and Administrative Meeting: Many Important Cases Resolved 78

Beijing Dispatch: The Supreme Court held its annual meeting and administrative meeting yesterday. The meeting was held downstairs in the newly built library of the court. The secretariat had made some arrangements beforehand. The opening ceremony was held at 9:00 AM. Guests included Xie Guansheng and Pan Enpei, secretaries and counselors of the Judicial Yuan, Mao Zuquan, president of the Administrative Court, and Zheng Lie, chief prosecutor of the Procuratorate, as well as the presidents, judges, chief clerks, and section chiefs of the civil and criminal courts of the court, totaling about 80 people. It was led by Court President Ju Zheng, who performed the ceremony as usual and delivered an opening speech, elaborating on the state of the judiciary in China. Next, Xie Guansheng gave a speech on the progress of the court's work in recent years, which was very detailed. After 10:00 AM, the annual meeting continued, chaired by Mr. Ju, and resolved many important cases, such as the allocation of duties for court presidents and judges of the court in 1934. It was originally scheduled to hold the administrative meeting immediately after the annual meeting, but because the weather was very hot in the afternoon and the attendees were sweating profusely, and the original work of the attendees had been slightly suspended due to the meeting, it was changed to continue at 8:00 AM today (the 8th). Today is a Sunday holiday, but because the meeting was very important for the reform of court affairs, it was still held by the chairman after consulting the opinions of the public, and all members attended. It is said that many important administrative cases were resolved. After the meeting, Court President Ju held a dinner for all the members in recognition of their hard work and to promote conversation. (8th)

Songjiang: The Director of National Tax Collection is Replaced 79

The collection of national taxes in this county is the responsibility of the first and second collection offices, which are divided according to the former jurisdictions of the Hua and Lou counties. Ye Runchun, the director of the first collection office, has held office for many years. Recently, he was suddenly accused by someone, and the Party Headquarters sent personnel to the county to check the accounts and ordered him to create a register for verification within a limited time. Mr. Ye also submitted his resignation, which was approved by the county government. Yang Yunwen was selected to take over the position and took over yesterday (the 8th). However, the accusations against Director Ye will probably not end easily.

New Police Chief Arrives in Songjiang 80

The newly appointed Police Chief He Yongyao, after being appointed, arrived in Songjiang from Shanghai by train at 9:00 AM this morning (the 9th). He was greeted by the police team at the station. The former chief, Zhou Ding, left Songjiang on the 1st to take over in Changshu. He sent personnel to handle the handover matters in this county. The new chief proceeded to handle the handover procedures immediately after arriving in Songjiang.

Haimen: A New Steamer Will Soon Sail on the Shanghai-Haimen Line 81

There are a total of five steamers operating on the Shanghai-Haimen line: Xin Renhe, Baohua, Daxing, Baofeng, and Guangxiang. All are doing well in business. Recently, Shi Xiangcheng and Xu Dechang from Chongming and others raised 150,000 yuan to order a new steamer from the Jiangnan Shipyard. It has been named Lichong and has been completed and launched. It is docked at the Shiliupu wharf in the south of Shanghai. It will be able to start operations as soon as the port and shipping bureau in this county is established.

The Epidemic is Rampant in Jinping Township 82

Since the beginning of summer, there has been a severe drought and no rain. The weather has been extremely hot. The temperature in the room has reached a maximum of 100 degrees Fahrenheit. Strong winds have blown during the day, suddenly turning cool. However, due to the erratic and variable weather, epidemics have been prevalent in the four townships. The day before yesterday, fifteen people died in Jinping Township in the sixth district in one day. The epidemic is rampant and continues to spread.

Wuxi: Drought Disaster Approaching, Relief Efforts Intensifying 83

This year's severe drought has already manifested as a disaster. At Zhangjing Bridge, only 30% of farmers are transplanting rice seedlings, while 70% are sitting and waiting. A small number, seeing no hope for rice cultivation, are switching to planting soybeans. Around Yangming Township, due to its proximity to Taihu Lake, 70% have already transplanted seedlings. However, due to the intense heat and lack of rain, the seedlings are developing slowly and mostly withering and turning yellow. The northern townships of Shitangwan and Luoshe are also suffering from severe drought and difficulty in drawing water. Therefore, they have gathered hundreds of farmers by gong to dredge the river at locations such as Li Kou, Qin Jia Zhuang Bridge, and Lin Bang Tou, diverting water from the Grand Canal to irrigate the fields. However, this can only temporarily save the already transplanted fields. The higher, unirrigated fields cannot be saved. On average, only 20-30% of the county has been able to transplant seedlings. If it doesn't rain again, even the already transplanted seedlings will wither and die, and the drought disaster will become immediately apparent. Currently, the farmers' worries are evident on their faces. In the Xicang area of the Second District, due to the drying up of the river, over 10,000 mu of farmland are likely to become completely barren. Therefore, Ji Guoyong, the Standing Committee member of the Fifth Branch of the Northern Jiangsu Experimental District in that area, instructed the Xicang Improvement Association to urge farmers to first pump water from the Grand Canal into the riverbank and then irrigate the fields. However, the project is massive and requires an estimated cost of over a thousand yuan, which cannot be raised immediately. The local villagers went to Changzhou to petition the county magistrate, Cai Ziping (who is from Xicang). Cai returned to his hometown the day before yesterday and convened a meeting with the district head, Yuan Yongshang, and others. As a result, it was decided to organize a pumping water committee for six townships, including Xicang, and appoint seven people, including Cai Zixing and Ji Guoyong, as committee members. Ten motorboats will be hired to pump water for disaster relief, with the costs shared by the farmers. Cai Ziping will be responsible for guaranteeing a temporary loan of 1,200 yuan from the Farmers Bank.

Changzhou: Dalai Rice Mill Burned Down 84

The Dalai Rice Mill, located below Huai De Bridge in Ximenwai, Wuyi County, caught fire at 1:00 PM on the 8th due to overheating of the engine steam pipe in the rear workshop. The fire quickly became extremely fierce. Although all the workers tried their best to extinguish it, it was difficult to put out because the river water was shallow. Later, fire brigades from various districts arrived to help, but most of the buildings had already been burned down. The fire was finally extinguished after about an hour. An investigation after the incident revealed that twenty-one workshop buildings and flour milling machinery were completely destroyed, resulting in significant losses.

Danyang: Change of Education Bureau Director 85

The Director of the Education Bureau in this county was previously concurrently held by County Magistrate Bi Jingqian. Now, due to the heavy burden of official duties, he is unable to continue in that role. He has resigned to the provincial government and recommended Gui Yinwu to fill the position. The Provincial Department of Education has approved the request and specially appointed Mr. Gui to take over. It is reported that the new director took office and affixed his seal yesterday.

Nantong: Provincial Order for Thorough Investigation of Yu Dong Militia 86

The provincial government has sent officials to Nantong and detained Chen Youqi, the head of Yu Dong District, and Ding Ziyan, the head of Yi Yu District, at the county government. Meanwhile, the county police force was dispatched to Yu Dong to surround the militia's firearms in Tangjiagou. The militia has made significant contributions to suppressing bandits and communists in the eastern townships in recent years, and all firearms have been inspected and branded. They refused to surrender their weapons, leading to a conflict between the two sides. Subsequently, mediation by local gentry resulted in the weapons not being surrendered for the time being. The militia turned over Tang Dazong, Jiang Zhaoxian, Tang Caizong, and Tang Xianchen to the city. On the 8th, they were sent to the provincial capital together with the two district heads, Chen and Ding, under the provincial order.
