Drought Disaster Seen in Nantong Prefecture 87

The counties under Nantong prefecture received thunderstorms earlier this month in some areas, but most areas still have not received rain. Rice and cotton crops are withering, and canals are drying up, creating an extremely dire situation.

Jiaxing: County Government Meeting to Relieve Drought Disaster 88

Due to the severe drought and lack of rain, causing fields to crack and rice seedlings to wither, the Jiaxing County Government convened a meeting of representatives from various agencies and organizations yesterday to discuss drought relief. The following resolutions were made: (1) In accordance with the provincial government's telegram, 20,000 yuan of local public funds will be allocated to purchase a number of water pumps to pump water from the large river into the branch rivers. (2) The original 9,000 yuan in machine loan funds held by the Farmers Bank will be used to purchase three horsepower engines to be lent to the people. (3) Eleven committee members will be appointed to form a drought relief committee to be specifically responsible for these tasks and facilitate progress. In addition, the gentry in the city have set up an altar to pray for rain and have observed a three-day ban on slaughter. Zhongxiu Town has initiated the use of water pumps to draw water from the outer river for residents to use, which has been implemented since the 10th. Moreover, ships at Cao Ting, Puguang Temple, and Xin Zha have mostly stopped sailing due to the drought.

Tenant Laborer Beats Landlord to Death 89

Hou Dingjiang, a farmer from Changtiaogang, Ru Ziwei, Third District, Jiaxing (originally from Jiangbei), cultivated nearly 100 mu of land and hired several workers to help with farming. Recently, due to the drought, the work of pumping water was intensified. Yesterday, a certain worker, exhausted and slack, was overly reprimanded by the landlord. In anger, the worker asked for a half-day break, which was refused, leading to a quarrel and then a physical fight. The worker struck Hou's waist with great force, causing serious injuries. He died that evening. The crowd arrested the murderer and reported the incident for an autopsy and punishment of the perpetrator.

Yangzhou: Villagers on Yangliu Road Block Construction of Culvert 90

The Yangliu Motor Road has been rushed to completion, and the construction of bridges and culverts is now actively underway. Construction has reached No. 141 at the Meijiagou site north of Xincheng in Yi County. This section of the river channel supplies water to the farmland, so a culvert needs to be built. The construction of a dam is currently underway, but around 3:00 PM on the 7th, suddenly over a hundred villagers came to block the dam construction, claiming that the culvert was too small and would obstruct the flow of river water to irrigate hundreds of miles of farmland in this township. If the water source is blocked and narrowed, it will greatly affect the farmland. The group demanded that the culvert be rebuilt as a bridge and dismantled the constructed dam on their own, preventing further construction. They intend to go to the county government to file a petition.

Gossip about the Expansion of the Yangzhou Movement 91

The book "Gossip about Yangzhou" written by Yi Junzuo, the compilation and review director of the Jiangsu Education Department, is considered by the people of Yangzhou to be deliberately slandering and insulting them, leading to unanimous opposition. It is now learned that the movement has expanded. The Jiangdu Women's Association believes that the insults to women in the book are particularly severe. Therefore, in accordance with Article 325, Paragraph 2, and Article 328 of the Criminal Law, Chairman Guo Jianren has been designated to file a private prosecution with the Zhenjiang District Court, scheduled to be heard on the 11th. A declaration has been issued to hold a citizens' assembly, and various small steamship companies have specially prepared six free ships to transport the public to the provincial capital to petition.

Hangzhou: Elderly Man Commits Suicide Due to Illness and Weariness of Life 92

Fu Songlin, who lives at No. 1 Jundusi Lane in this city, is 51 years old and works in the second-hand goods business. Recently, due to poverty and illness, he suddenly had the idea of suicide. At 8:00 AM yesterday, after changing clothes and bathing, he secretly hanged himself to death. The local Public Security Bureau reported the incident to the court for inspection.

Sleeping on Tracks to Cool Off, Crushed to Death by Train 93

Xia Caixi, a farmer living in Yaodian Bridge outside Genshan Gate in this city, could not sleep comfortably at home the night before last due to the hot weather. He had a whimsical idea to sleep on the railroad tracks to cool off. As a result, he was run over by a Shanghai-Hangzhou freight train, crushed into three sections, with blood and flesh blurred beyond recognition.

Fire Brigade Fire Truck Causes Major Disaster 94

The pump truck of the Public Security Bureau Fire Brigade of the provincial capital was returning to the team from fighting a fire at Gongchen Bridge at 5:00 PM yesterday. When passing the corner of Yanling Road and Pinghai Road, it collided with a certain school's car, injuring over a dozen people on both sides, four of whom were seriously injured and sent to Guangji Hospital for treatment.

Special Article

Draft Review and Amendment of the Constitution of the Republic of China 95

The National Assembly of the Republic of China, entrusted by all the people, following the teachings of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the founder of the Republic of China, hereby enacts this Constitution, promulgates it throughout the country, and pledges eternal compliance.

Chapter 1: General Principles 96

Article 1: The Republic of China is a republic based on the Three Principles of the People.

Article 2: The sovereignty of the Republic of China belongs to all the people.

Article 3: Those possessing the nationality of the Republic of China are citizens of the Republic of China.

Article 4: The territory of the Republic of China includes Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, Sichuan, Xikang, Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Qinghai, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, Chahar, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Xinjiang, Mongolia, Tibet, and other inherent territories. The territory of the Republic of China shall not be altered without a resolution of the National Assembly.

Article 5: All ethnic groups of the Republic of China are constituent members of the Chinese nation and are equal in status.

Article 6: The national flag of the Republic of China is defined as a red field with a white sun in a blue sky in the upper left corner.

Article 7: The capital of the Republic of China is located in Nanjing.

Chapter 2: Rights and Obligations of the People 97

Article 8: All citizens of the Republic of China are equal under the law.

Article 9: The people have freedom of person. They shall not be arrested, detained, interrogated, or punished except in accordance with the law.

Anyone arrested or detained on suspicion of a crime shall be immediately informed by the executing agency of the reasons for the arrest or detention, as well as their relatives, and shall be transferred to the competent court for interrogation within 24 hours at the latest. The person or another may also petition the competent court to submit them for interrogation to the executing agency within 24 hours.

The court shall not refuse the petition mentioned in the preceding paragraph, and the executing agency shall not refuse the court's submission for interrogation.

Article 10: Except for active-duty military personnel, the people shall not be subject to military trials.

Article 11: The people have the freedom of residence. Their places of residence shall not be entered, searched, or sealed without legal basis.

Article 12: The people have the freedom of movement. They shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 13: The people have the freedom of speech, writing, and publication. They shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 14: The people have the freedom of secret communication. They shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 15: The people have the freedom of religious belief. They shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 16: The people have the freedom of assembly and association. They shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law.

Article 17: The property of the people shall not be requisitioned, confiscated, sealed, or confiscated except in accordance with the law.

Article 18: The people have the right to petition, appeal, and litigate in accordance with the law.

Article 19: The people have the right to elect, recall, initiate, and referendum in accordance with the law.

Article 20: The people have the right to take examinations in accordance with the law.

Article 21: The people have the obligation to pay taxes in accordance with the law.

Article 22: The people have the obligation to perform military service in accordance with the law.

Article 23: The people have the obligation to perform public service in accordance with the law.

Article 24: All other freedoms and rights of the people, which do not prejudice social order and public interest, are protected by the Constitution.

Article 25: Laws restricting the freedoms or rights of the people shall be limited to what is necessary to safeguard national security, avoid imminent danger, maintain social order, or promote public interest.

Article 26: Public officials who violate the law and infringe upon the freedoms or powers of the people shall be held criminally and civilly liable, in addition to being disciplined in accordance with the law. The injured people may also seek compensation from the state in accordance with the law for the damages they have suffered.

Chapter 3: National Assembly 98

Article 27: The National Assembly is composed of the following national representatives:

1. Each county and city and its equivalent area shall elect one representative. However, for populations exceeding 300,000, one additional representative shall be elected for every additional 500,000 people.

The equivalent areas of counties and cities shall be determined by law.

2. Representatives shall be elected from Mongolia and Xinjiang, and the number shall be determined by law.

3. Nationals residing abroad shall elect representatives, and the number shall be determined by law.

Article 28: The election of national representatives shall be conducted by means of universal, equal, direct, and secret ballot.

Article 29: Citizens of the Republic of China who have reached the age of twenty have the right to elect representatives in accordance with the law, and those who have reached the age of twenty-five have the right to be elected as representatives in accordance with the law.

Article 30: The term of office of national representatives is four years.

If a national representative violates the law or neglects their duties, the original electoral district may re-elect them in accordance with the law.

Article 31: The National Assembly shall convene once every two years for a session of one month. If necessary, it may be extended by one month.

The National Assembly may convene a temporary National Assembly with the consent of more than one-quarter of the representatives.

Article 32: The functions of the National Assembly are as follows:

1. Elect and recall the President, Vice President, and the heads of the Legislative, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuan, as well as members of the Legislative Yuan and Control Yuan (This clause is reserved for further discussion by the Yuan).

2. Initiate legislative principles.

3. Revise budget proposals, declarations of war, peace treaties, laws, treaties, martial law, and amnesty. The exercise of the power of revision shall be limited to determining whether or not it is possible.

4. Receive reports from the President and the Legislative, Examination, and Control Yuan.

5. Handle matters submitted by the President and the Legislative, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuan for resolution.

6. Other powers conferred by the Constitution.

Article 33: National representatives shall not exercise their powers during the recess of the National Assembly, unless otherwise stipulated in the Constitution.

Article 34: National representatives shall not be held responsible to the outside world for their speeches and votes made at the meeting.

Article 35: Except for those caught in the act, national representatives shall not be arrested or detained during the session without the permission of the National Assembly.

Article 36: During the recess of the National Assembly, a National Assembly Committee shall be established. Its members shall be mutually elected by the national representatives in accordance with the following provisions:

1. Provinces with a population of less than 5 million shall each have two national representatives mutually elected. Those with more than 5 million but less than 10 million shall mutually elect three people. Those with more than 10 million but less than 20 million shall mutually elect four people. Those with more than 20 million but less than 30 million shall mutually elect five people. Those with more than 30 million or more shall mutually elect six people.

2. National representatives from Mongolia and Tibet shall each mutually elect three people.

3. The national representatives elected by nationals residing abroad shall mutually elect three people.

Article 37: The term of office of the members of the National Assembly Committee shall be from the date of the adjournment of the National Assembly until the date of the convening of the next National Assembly.

Article 38: The functions of the National Assembly Committee are as follows:

1. Take over the Secretariat of the National Assembly.

2. Prepare for the convening of the next National Assembly and temporary National Assemblies.

3. Revise, on behalf of the National Assembly, budget proposals, declarations of war, peace treaties, treaties, martial law, and amnesties passed by the Legislative Yuan.

4. Handle, on behalf of the National Assembly, matters submitted by the President and the Legislative, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuan for resolution.

5. Accept impeachments by the Control Yuan against the President, Vice President, the heads of the Legislative, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuan, and members of the Legislative Yuan and Control Yuan. When the National Assembly Committee resolves to accept an impeachment case by the Control Yuan against the President, Vice President, and the heads of the Legislative, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuan, it shall immediately convene a temporary National Assembly to decide whether or not to remove them. When the National Assembly Committee resolves to accept an impeachment case by the Control Yuan against members of the Legislative Yuan and Control Yuan, the impeached members shall be immediately dismissed.

6. When the National Assembly Committee considers that a national policy or administrative measure is inappropriate, it may submit inquiries to the President.

If the National Assembly Committee is not satisfied with the President's response, it may, with the attendance of more than two-thirds of all members and the approval of more than two-thirds of the members present, convene a temporary National Assembly to decide whether or not to remove the President.

7. Other powers conferred by the Constitution.

Article 39: Members of the National Assembly Committee shall not hold other public office or conduct business concurrently.

Article 40: If a member of the National Assembly Committee violates the law or neglects their duties, they shall be re-elected by the national representatives who originally mutually elected them.

Article 41: The organization of the National Assembly and the election of national representatives, the organization of the National Assembly Committee, and the election of the members of the National Assembly Committee shall be determined by law.

Chapter Four: The Central Government, Section One: The President 99

Article 42: The President is the head of state and represents the Republic of China in foreign affairs.

Article 43: The President promulgates laws and issues orders according to law, which must be countersigned by the heads of the relevant Yuan (branches of government).

Article 44: The President commands the national army, navy, and air force according to law.

Article 45: The President exercises the power to declare war, negotiate peace, and conclude treaties according to law.

Article 46: The President declares and lifts martial law according to law.

Article 47: The President exercises the power to grant general amnesties, special pardons, reductions of sentences, and restoration of rights according to law.

Article 48: The President, before promulgating budget bills, declarations of war, peace treaties, treaty bills, martial law bills, and amnesty bills resolved by the Legislative Yuan, shall submit them to the National Assembly or the National Assembly Committee for reconsideration.

Article 49: The President appoints and removes civil and military officials according to law.

Article 50: The President confers honors according to law.

Article 51: The President concurrently serves as the head of the executive branch and oversees all executive power.

Article 52: The President is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 53: Citizens of the Republic of China who are at least forty years old may be elected as President and Vice President.

Article 54: Active military personnel may not be elected as President or Vice President.

Article 55: The term of office for the President and Vice President is four years, and they may be re-elected for one consecutive term.

Article 57: The President shall take an oath to the nation on the day of inauguration, with the oath as follows:

(I, with utmost sincerity, swear to the nation that I will be loyal and do my utmost to abide by the Constitution, and in accordance with the powers conferred upon me by the Constitution, to execute national laws, safeguard the unity and independence of the Republic of China, so as not to betray the trust of the people. Should I violate the law or neglect my duties, I am willing to be sanctioned by the people. So I swear.)

Article 58: If the President is unable to perform duties due to circumstances, the Vice President shall act on his/her behalf. If both the President and Vice President are unable to perform duties, the head of the Executive Yuan shall act on his/her behalf.

Article 59: The President shall be relieved of duties on the date of the expiration of the term. If the next President has not yet been elected or has not yet taken office upon the expiration of the term, the powers of the President shall be temporarily exercised by the head of the Executive Yuan.

Article 60: In accordance with the provisions of the preceding article, when the head of the Executive Yuan acts on behalf of the President, the term shall not exceed six months.

Article 61: Except for committing offenses of internal rebellion or treason, the President shall not be subject to criminal prosecution unless impeached or dismissed.

Section Two: The Executive Yuan

Article 62: The Executive Yuan is the highest organ of the central government for exercising executive power.

Article 63: The Executive Yuan shall have one President and twenty Ministers without Portfolio, who shall be appointed and removed by the President.

Article 64: The Executive Yuan shall establish ministries and commissions to manage national administrative functions.

Article 65: The ministers of the various ministries and the chairpersons of the various commissions of the Executive Yuan shall be selected, appointed, and dismissed by the President from among the Ministers without Portfolio.

Article 66: The President of the Executive Yuan, the Ministers without Portfolio, the ministers of the various ministries, and the chairpersons of the various commissions are responsible to the President.

Article 67: The Executive Yuan shall establish an Executive Council, which shall be composed of the President, the President of the Executive Yuan, and the Ministers without Portfolio, with the President as the chairperson. If the President is unable to attend due to circumstances, the President of the Executive Yuan shall serve as the chairperson.

Article 68: The following matters shall be resolved by the Executive Council:

1. Legislative bills and budget bills submitted to the Legislative Yuan.

2. Martial law bills and amnesty bills submitted to the Legislative Yuan.

3. Declarations of war, peace treaties, treaty bills, and other important international matters submitted to the Legislative Yuan.

4. Matters proposed by the Ministers without Portfolio, ministries, and commissions.

5. Matters of common concern among the ministries and commissions.

6. Matters referred for discussion by the President or the President of the Executive Yuan.

Article 69: The organization of the Executive Yuan shall be determined by law.

Section Three: The Legislative Yuan

Article 70: The Legislative Yuan is the highest organ of the central government for exercising legislative power and is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 71: The Legislative Yuan has the power to resolve legislative bills, budget bills, martial law bills, amnesty bills, declarations of war, peace treaties, treaty bills, and other important international matters.

Article 72: The Legislative Yuan shall have one President, with a term of four years, and may be re-elected.

Article 73: During the adjournment of the National Assembly, if the President of the Legislative Yuan leaves office due to circumstances, the legislators shall elect an acting President from among themselves, but it must be approved by the National Assembly Committee.

Article 74: Legislators shall be elected in accordance with the following provisions: 1. Three representatives shall be elected from each province by the National Assembly provincial representatives, and three representatives shall be elected from Mongolia, Tibet, and citizens residing abroad by the National Assembly representatives, and the candidates are not limited to the National Assembly representatives or the people of the respective provinces and regions.

2. The President of the Legislative Yuan shall select talents with specialized knowledge and experience and submit them to the National Assembly or the National Assembly Committee for final election. The number of such persons shall not exceed one-third of the total number in the preceding paragraph.

Article 75: The term of office for legislators is four years, and they may be re-elected.

Article 76: The Executive, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuans may submit bills to the Legislative Yuan regarding matters under their jurisdiction.

Article 77: The President may submit a legislative bill resolved by the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration before its promulgation.

If the Legislative Yuan maintains the original bill after reconsideration by a two-thirds majority of the attending legislators, the President shall promulgate it immediately.

Article 78: The National Assembly may reconsider laws after their promulgation.

Article 79: The President shall promulgate legislative bills submitted by the Legislative Yuan for promulgation within fifteen days after the bill arrives. Bills reconsidered by the National Assembly or the National Assembly Committee shall be promulgated within fifteen days after receiving the notice of reconsideration.

Article 80: Legislators shall not be held responsible for their speeches and votes within the Yuan.

Article 81: Except in cases of flagrant offenses, legislators may not be arrested or detained without the permission of the Legislative Yuan.

Article 82: Legislators may not concurrently hold other public offices or engage in business.

Article 83: The election of legislators and the organization of the Legislative Yuan shall be determined by law.

Section Four: The Judicial Yuan

Article 84: The Judicial Yuan is the highest organ of the central government for exercising judicial power.

Article 85: The Judicial Yuan shall have one President, with a term of four years, and may be re-elected.

The President of the Judicial Yuan is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 86: During the adjournment of the National Assembly, if the President of the Judicial Yuan leaves office due to circumstances, the National Assembly Committee shall elect an acting President.

Article 87: The Judicial Yuan shall establish a Supreme Court, a Committee on the Discipline of Public Functionaries, and a Ministry of Judicial Administration.

Article 88: The President of the Supreme Court, the Chairperson of the Committee on the Discipline of Public Functionaries, and the Minister of Judicial Administration shall be nominated by the President of the Judicial Yuan in accordance with the law and submitted to the President for appointment and removal.

Article 89: Matters concerning special pardons, reductions of sentences, and restoration of rights shall be submitted by the President of the Judicial Yuan to the President for action in accordance with the law.

Article 90: Courts shall accept civil, criminal, administrative, and all other lawsuits and non-lawsuit cases in accordance with the law.

Article 91: The Supreme Court has the power to unify the interpretation of laws and orders.

Article 92: Judges shall conduct trials independently in accordance with the law.

Article 93: Judges may not be dismissed unless they are sentenced to criminal punishment or disciplinary action, or declared bankrupt. They may not be suspended, transferred, or have their salaries reduced without legal basis.

Article 94: The organization of the Judicial Yuan and the organization of the courts shall be determined by law.

Section Five: The Examination Yuan

Article 95: The Examination Yuan is the highest organ of the central government for exercising the power of examination and personnel administration.

Article 96: The Examination Yuan shall have one President, with a term of four years, and may be re-elected.

The President of the Examination Yuan is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 97: During the adjournment of the National Assembly, if the President of the Examination Yuan leaves office due to circumstances, the National Assembly Committee shall elect an acting President.

Article 98: The Examination Yuan shall establish a Ministry of Personnel Administration and submit it to the President for appointment and removal after holding an examination.

The Chairperson and members of the Examination Committee shall be appointed by the President upon the recommendation of the President of the Examination Yuan in accordance with the law.

Article 100: The following qualifications shall be determined by the Examination Yuan through examination:

1. Qualifications for appointment of civil servants.

2. Qualifications for candidates for public office.

3. Qualifications for practicing specialized professions or technical personnel.

Article 101: The organization of the Examination Yuan shall be determined by law.

Section Six: The Control Yuan

Article 102: The Control Yuan is the highest organ of the central government for exercising the power of control, overseeing impeachment and auditing, and is responsible to the National Assembly.

Article 103: The Control Yuan shall have one President, with a term of four years, and may be re-elected.

Article 104: During the adjournment of the National Assembly, if the President of the Control Yuan leaves office due to circumstances, the members of the Control Yuan shall elect an acting President from among themselves, but it must be approved by the National Assembly Committee.

Article 105: Members of the Control Committee shall be elected by the National Assembly representatives from each province (two representatives from each province), and by the National Assembly representatives elected from Mongolia, Tibet, and citizens residing abroad (two representatives from each region). The candidates are not limited to the National Assembly representatives.

Article 106: The term of office for members of the Control Committee is four years, and they may be re-elected.

Article 107: When central and local civil servants violate the law or neglect their duties, the Control Committee shall initiate impeachment proceedings in accordance with the following provisions:

1. Impeachment cases against the President and Vice President must be proposed by ten or more members of the Inspection Committee and jointly signed by more than one-half of all members of the Control Committee.

2. Impeachment cases against the Presidents of the Executive, Legislative, Judicial, Examination, and Control Yuans must be proposed by five or more members of the Control Committee and jointly signed by more than one-third of all members of the Control Committee.

3. Impeachment cases against Ministers without Portfolio, ministers of the various ministries of the Executive Yuan, chairpersons of the various commissions, legislators, and members of the Control Committee must be proposed by two or more members of the Control Committee and jointly signed by five or more members.

4. Impeachment cases against other civil servants must be proposed by one or more members of the Control Committee and jointly signed by three or more members.

Article 108: Impeachment cases shall be submitted to the Committee on the Discipline of Public Functionaries, unless otherwise specified in the Constitution for the accepting authority.

Article 109: When the Committee on the Discipline of Public Functionaries decides that the impeached person should be dismissed or subjected to other disciplinary actions, the President or the responsible superior shall execute the decision.

Article 110: The procedures for initiating impeachment against active-duty military officers, the accepting authority, and disciplinary measures shall be determined by law.

Article 111: The Control Yuan shall establish an Auditing Committee to manage auditing and inspection matters.

Article 112: The Auditing Committee shall have one Chairperson and six members of the Auditing Committee, who shall be nominated by the President of the Control Yuan in accordance with the law and submitted to the President for appointment and removal.

Article 113: The Auditing Committee's final accounts report shall be reviewed by the plenary session of the Control Yuan and promulgated in accordance with the law.

Article 114: Members of the Control Committee shall not be held responsible for their speeches and votes within the Yuan.

Article 115: Except in cases of flagrant offenses, members of the Control Committee may not be arrested or detained without the permission of the Control Yuan.

Article 116: Members of the Control Committee may not concurrently hold other public offices or engage in business.

Article 117: The election of members of the Control Committee and the organization of the Control Yuan shall be determined by law.

Local News

Commemoration of the Northern Expedition Pledge Ceremony: All Sectors Held a Commemorative Meeting Yesterday. Over One Hundred Representatives from All Sectors Attended. Tao Baichuan Reported on the Significance of the Commemoration. 100

Yesterday (the 9th) was the anniversary of the National Revolutionary Army's pledge to launch the Northern Expedition. Representatives from all sectors of the city gathered at the City Party Headquarters auditorium at 9:00 AM to hold a commemorative meeting. Those present included Tao Baichuan from the City Party Headquarters, Xiong Lixian from the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, Li Zemin from the City Public Security Bureau, Qiu Yunming from the Land Bureau, Wang Zongjian from the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office, Zhou Feicheng from the City Education Association, Yu Zhenhui from the City Farmers' Association, Lin Kecong from the Women's National Goods Year Movement, Pan Rongting from the South Shanghai District Farmers' Association, Xu Chonghua from the Chinese Youth Association, Li Shiyong from the City Cooperative Business Promotion Association, Yu Jiugao from the Wharf Business Office, Yin Yong from the Youth Propaganda Team, Wu Jianzhi from the Anhui Association of Students in Shanghai, Chen Bangyan from New Asia Middle School, Zhang Jingyi from the Patriotic Girls' School, Li Julin from Jiangjing Elementary School, Yin Zhiren from Cheng Elementary School, and over two hundred representatives from various institutions, organizations, schools, and party headquarters. After performing the ceremonial rites, Chairman Tao Baichuan gave a report, stating that the Republic of China has two important commemorative dates: October 10th and July 9th. The former is the National Day, and the latter is the Restoration Day. Without October 10th, China would not have today's democratic republic. However, without the Northern Expedition launched on July 9th to restore the Republic of China, the country would no longer be a country, and even a democratic republic would not have much significance. The reason why the July 9th Northern Expedition was able to achieve the effect of restoring China was primarily because of the guidance of the Three Principles of the People, the leadership of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, the sacrifice and struggle of loyal and brave soldiers, the planning and assistance of the Chinese Kuomintang Party Headquarters, and the practical cooperation of the people. With these five reasons, the Northern Expedition was able to be completed quickly. However, we should understand that the completion of the Northern Expedition is only the beginning of the revolution, not the completion of the revolution. The completion of the Northern Expedition is still far from the completion of the revolution, because the revolution of the Three Principles of the People, in terms of nationalism, requires the abolition of unequal treaties in order to seek equality in international status; in terms of democracy, it requires the implementation of local self-government in order to seek equality in political status; and in terms of people's livelihood, it requires equalization of land ownership and regulation of capital in order to seek equality in economic status. All of this cannot be achieved by the Northern Expedition alone, and requires our continued efforts. Therefore, it is said that the revolution has not yet been completed, and comrades must continue to work hard. People doubt and are disappointed in the revolution because they believe that the completion of the Northern Expedition is the completion of the revolution. Therefore, we must clearly recognize this point in the future and continue the work of the revolution. The path of our efforts should first be to unite as one and build a unified, strong central government, and support and supervise it. The declaration of the Northern Expedition stated that the purpose of the Northern Expedition was to build a unified government as the foundation for overthrowing imperialism. We must strive to realize this requirement. Second, under the leadership of this unified government, we should restore the work of the military administration period, continue the work of the political tutelage period, and begin the work of the constitutional government period. However, what we call the military administration period here is external, not internal. It is aimed at international enemies and engages in national defense construction. All facilities should be centered on external military affairs in order to recover lost territories and revive the nation. At the same time, in order to seek closer cooperation from the people, we should keep our promise to formulate a constitution as scheduled, begin the constitutional government period, and continue the work of political tutelage and construction under the leadership of the elected government, in order to thoroughly complete the Three Principles of the People. If so, the achievements of the Northern Expedition will not be lost, and the Northern Expedition will be more meaningful.

The River Dries Up, Traffic is Blocked, Rice Prices Rise Sharply Again Yesterday, from Eleven Yuan to Eleven Yuan and Eight Jiao 101

The recent severe drought in various parts of Jiangnan has caused disasters. This year's poor harvest is a foregone conclusion. In addition, the inland river has dried up, and there are few ships, so there is a severe shortage of rice coming to Shanghai. As a result, rice merchants hoard goods and prices have risen sharply. The day before yesterday, it had risen from ten yuan to eleven yuan and two jiao. Yesterday, due to the lack of rice arrivals, it rose another six jiao, reaching eleven yuan and eight jiao per dan. The authorities have already paid attention to this, it is said.

The Eurasia Aviation Corporation's Northwest route was suspended more than a year ago due to the war in Xinjiang Province. The company believes that the war in the province has ended and that the Eurasia joint transportation needs to be completed urgently. Therefore, Li Jingcong, the general manager of the company, sent a telegram to Sheng Shicai, the local authority of the province, requesting the Eurasia aircraft to reach Dihua and Tacheng in order to complete the Eurasia route as soon as possible. Li also planned to personally discuss all matters related to the resumption of flights. It has been more than a month since the telegram was sent, and inquiries have been made, but no reply has been received. Therefore, the company sent another telegram to inquire the day before yesterday. Once a reply is received, Li will fly to Dihua to meet with Sheng to discuss the resumption of flights. If no reply is received, the situation will be reported to the Ministry of Transportation for instructions so that the Eurasia route can be completed as soon as possible. The China Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Guangdong route has been suspended for a month due to a plane crash. The company is now actively preparing to resume flights in order to facilitate passengers because the transportation between Shanghai and Guangdong is very busy. As for the two new aircraft ordered from the United States, they are already on their way and will arrive in Shanghai for assembly at the end of this month. Tianjin Municipality: Concurrent Levy of Business Tax on Floating Capital; Chamber of Commerce Telegraphs Ministry of Finance to Request Rectification 116

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing to request the Ministry to instruct the Tianjin Municipal Business Tax Collection Office to rectify the concurrent levy of business tax on floating capital. The original telegram stated (omitting titles): “Upon investigating the business tax in this city since its implementation, the investigation and taxation have often been uneven, leading to disputes over the years. The most serious issue is the treatment of floating capital, which is of utmost importance. Floating capital originally belongs to the commercial transactions of shops, representing temporary loans that are repaid later. It is fundamentally different from fixed capital and public reserve funds and should not be included in capital taxation. However, the Tianjin Municipal Business Tax Collection Office insists that floating capital is used for business purposes and invokes the collection regulations of provinces and cities such as Pingjin, Zhejiang, and Jiangxi, all of which explicitly stipulate taxation. Despite repeated arguments, no effect has been achieved. Such forced analogies and arbitrary references are unreasonable. In addition to continuing to strongly argue, this matter concerns the interests of merchants nationwide. We specifically telegraph your association, hoping you will investigate and promptly telegraph the Ministry of Finance to quickly rectify and stop this practice.” Accordingly, we respectfully submit this telegram to your ministry for review, earnestly requesting prompt approval for the Hebei Provincial Department of Finance to rectify this issue to resolve disputes. With utmost sincerity, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce respectfully submits this.”

Domestic Cement Prices Drop to Promote Sales; Daily Sales Exceed 5,000 Barrels; More Than Double the Previous Amount 117

Since the aggressive dumping of foreign cement in our country, the domestic cement industry has suffered severe setbacks. Recently, Chinese merchants have collectively reduced prices to compete and counter foreign goods. Since the beginning of summer, sales have suddenly become brisk. The details are as follows:

Unified Price Reductions: According to sources in the cement industry, domestic cement manufacturers have uniformly reduced prices to compete with foreign cement. Elephant brand is sold for $6.30 per barrel, Horse brand for $6.25, and sack heads for $2.45 per bag. Foreign cement companies are also considering following suit. However, many wholesalers secretly increase the marked price slightly or offer lower prices.

Brisk Sales: According to Mr. Wang of the National Cement Industry Federation, speaking to a reporter from the Ta Kung Pao, cement sales have suddenly surged since the beginning of summer. The original sales volume was only 2,000 to 3,000 barrels per day, but recently it has skyrocketed to 5,000 to 6,000 barrels, an increase of more than double. Cement companies like Qixing Huashang are experiencing a situation where supply cannot meet demand. The reason for the brisk sales is that many provinces are actively engaged in constructing highways, bridges, and various construction projects, leading to a surge in orders from Shanghai cement factories, resulting in this large sales volume.

Commissioning He Bingxian to Proceed with Expanding the Nanyang Market for Domestic Goods, Following the Ministry's Four Principles 118

Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo, upon returning from an inspection of industries in Nanyang, immediately began actively planning to develop the Nanyang market for domestic goods. According to sources from the International Trade Bureau, Minister Chen is most concerned about the outward development of domestic goods. Overseas Chinese in Nanyang are also eager for domestic goods to be shipped and sold there to prevent the outflow of profits. If this measure is implemented, it will greatly benefit the national economy and the people's livelihood. Minister Chen has now commissioned He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau, to be responsible for carrying out this task. The purpose of the development is to promote the sale of our country's excellent local products as much as possible. The Ministry has formulated four principles to be implemented step by step: (1) Standardization of production; (2) Reduction of costs; (3) Attention to international market conditions; (4) Focus on international promotion. After receiving the order, the International Trade Bureau will convene domestic goods manufacturers in this city to discuss implementation methods according to the principles set by the Ministry.

Page 12

After the Implementation of the Savings Bank Law, the Rural Economy is Expected to Recover 122

Current Funds in Various Banks Amount to 60 Million Circulating in Rural Areas

Banking Circles Studying Methods to Form a Rural Lending Syndicate

The Savings Bank Law has been passed by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the National Government on July 4th. Article 8 of the law stipulates that savings banks' collateral loans to rural cooperatives and loans secured by agricultural products shall not be less than one-fifth of the total deposits. A reporter from the Shen Shi News inquired with banking circles yesterday. There are currently sixteen savings banks and ordinary banks that also handle savings deposits in Shanghai. As of the end of 1933, their total deposits amounted to 263.521 million yuan. Combined with the deposits received by other financial institutions that do not have specialized savings departments, the total should not be less than 300 million yuan. One-fifth of this amount is 60 million yuan. After the implementation of this law, savings banks will have significant development in lending to cooperatives, agricultural warehouses, and agricultural mortgage lending in various regions. The cash that has concentrated in urban areas in recent years may thus flow back to rural areas, which may bring hope for the recovery of the financially depleted rural economy. However, the banking circles are currently engaged in practical and organizational research on how various banks can cooperate to achieve real results. According to the proposal of Mr. Jin Guobao of the Bank of Communications, a rural lending cooperative syndicate should be organized by various banks to formulate a comprehensive plan for various provinces and regions, to avoid the drawbacks of competitive lending by various banks, and to extend to remote provinces, without being biased towards the southeast region.

The Shanghai-Wuxi Highway Surface is Completed; Actively Constructing Bridges Across Rivers; A Total of More Than Eighty Bridges on the Entire Line; Expected to be Completed by the End of July 126

Shanghai-Wuxi Long-Distance Bus Company’s Share Subscription is Enthusiastic

The Jiangsu Provincial Government's Department of Construction began construction of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway in sections, starting on April 20th of this year. The road surface of the entire line, more than 200 li, has been paved. Bridges across rivers are now being actively constructed. The long-distance bus company, organized by Shanghai and Wuxi gentry and merchants, is seeing very enthusiastic share subscriptions. Details are recorded separately below.

Pavement Completed 127

The designated route of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway starts from Baoshan Road in Shanghai, passing through Zhenru, Nanxiang, Jiading, Taicang, Changshu, to Wuxi, with a total length of more than 230 li for the trunk road. There is another branch line from Changshu to Suzhou, which is more than 80 li. After the Provincial Department of Construction raised sufficient funds by pre-paying road rental fees to the Shanghai banking group and the Shanghai-Wuxi Long-Distance Bus Company Preparatory Office, construction began in sections. The pavement at each station is laid with coal cinder and yellow sand and has been completed.

Bridge Construction 128

Regarding the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway, there are more than 80 large and small bridges at various stations along the entire line. The bridges from Shanghai to Kunshan were started simultaneously during the paving of the road surface, and most have been completed. However, the bridges across the rivers in the two sections from Wuxi to Changshu and from Suzhou to Changshu on the branch road are still under construction. Because the highway bridges are intended for future use by buses, the construction must be solid, so the implementation of the project is more time-consuming and difficult. It is expected to be completed by the end of July.

Enthusiastic Subscription 129

Shanghai and Wuxi gentry and merchants Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, Rong Zongjing, Shi Liangcai, etc., initiated the organization of the Shanghai-Wuxi Long-Distance Bus Company, with capital set at one million yuan, divided into 100,000 shares, each share worth ten yuan. The preparatory meeting decided that the initiators would raise the funds themselves, and then proceed separately. By the end of last month, the total number of shares subscribed had reached 650,000 yuan. Tenders will be invited in the middle of next month to order more than 20 of the latest long-distance buses. Yesterday, a reporter from the Ta Kung Pao inquired at the Shanghai Preparatory Office on Jiangxi Road, and the official opening date for the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway long-distance bus service is expected to be within ten days of this year.

Beijing-Shanghai Long-Distance Telephone; Yesterday a Trial Conversation Between Yuyao and Shanghai; The Sound Wave of the Trial Conversation Was Very Clear; The Entire Beijing-Shanghai Line Will Be Completed Next Month 130

The nine-province long-distance telephone project organized by the Ministry of Communications is actively underway. The four groups of personnel, under the sweltering heat, urged the craftsmen to speed up their work. The two wires hung in the Beijing-Zhenjiang, Wuxi-Yuyao, and Shanghai-Yuyao sections have been completed successively. The Zhenjiang-Wuxi section is expected to be completed the day after tomorrow. The commissioner of supervision for the entire line and engineer of the Shanghai-Yuyao section, Bao Liyan, telegraphed to invite the engineers of each section to meet in Wuxi to discuss coordination methods in order to complete the project as soon as possible. Yesterday, they traveled from Yuyao to Wuxi and met with Chen Xiang and Lu Bingzhang, the engineers of the Wuxi-Zhenjiang-Yuyao section, who had been waiting there. Zhao Lisheng of the Beijing-Zhenjiang section, due to the urgency of the project, had already proceeded ahead to understand the project progress and economic situation in detail. Yesterday, he telegraphed to the long-distance telephone office of the telegraph bureau to conduct a trial conversation between Yuyao and Shanghai. It was heard that the sound wave was very clear, and the results were very satisfactory. The entire Beijing-Shanghai line is expected to be fully connected within the next month.

Joint Beijing-Shanghai-Pukou Train Service; No Need to Change Locomotives to Cross the River; Passengers are Picked Up by Rented Cars 131

According to the Huadong News Agency, since the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and the Tianjin-Pukou Railway implemented a joint transportation service on the 1st of this month, in order to facilitate passenger transport and save locomotive power between Nanjing Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Line and Xiaguan Station on the Tianjin-Pukou Line, there is no need to change locomotives and drag them to the Coal Wharf. Instead, passengers are picked up and dropped off by rented cars. All car expenses are borne jointly by both parties. It has also been approved by the transportation offices of the two railways, and the transportation office of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway agreed that in addition to the connection of the second and fourth trains of the Beijing-Shanghai Line and the eighth and sixth trains of the Tianjin-Pukou Line, the third zero five and twenty-first trains of the Tianjin-Pukou Line will also be added for connection. After consultation between the two parties, the cars of the Jiangnan Automobile Company will be used. The company's original price was eight yuan per hour. Now, in order to develop the business of joint transportation passenger business, it has been approved to reduce it to three yuan per hour, and ten articles of measures have been signed, which will be implemented from the day before yesterday for a trial period of six months.

Committee Meeting of the County Anti-Smoking Association; Regulations for the Number and Grades of Opium Paste Shops in Each District 134

Since its establishment, the Shanghai County Anti-Smoking Committee has handled the registration of opium paste shops and smoking houses. As of the end of June, the registered establishments include two opium paste shops and one smoking house in Minhang; one opium paste shop and one smoking house in Maqiao. In addition, 19 smokers have voluntarily requested to quit smoking and have been sent to Shanghai hospitals for treatment. The committee held its fourth meeting yesterday, chaired by Chairman Pan Zhongjia. The chairman first reported on the progress, and then discussed various proposals. (1) The county's smokers have been successively applying for the registration of opium paste shops according to the number and grade of establishments. It is proposed to review and approve this first, so that it can be submitted for registration. (2) How many smoking houses should be set up in the county, and how should the location be reviewed and approved for application? Resolution: Both proposals were discussed together. It was resolved that (1) Each district should apply to set up one opium paste shop, with a maximum of two. Minhang is designated as Grade C, and the other districts are designated as Grade D. (2) Most of the county's residents are poor. Each town in the township where the market is located may set up one or two smoking houses. Minhang is designated as Grade B, and the others are designated as Grade C. (3) Investigate the smokers in each district, and propose to extend the deadline for completion of the investigation to before July 15. Resolution: Passed, and the Public Security Bureau is instructed to instruct the sub-bureaus and stations to report within the deadline. (4) How should the anti-smoking campaign be continued during the prescribed period for smoker registration? Resolution: Print and distribute the anti-smoking regulations for widespread publicity. At the same time, issue separate orders to each district and the Public Security Bureau to conduct thorough publicity. Also, a temporary motion was proposed by the chairman for deliberation: Should the committee send personnel to Shanghai hospitals to visit smokers who voluntarily requested to quit smoking? Resolution: The meeting will send personnel to investigate and offer condolences.

The Yu-Ping Railway; Groundbreaking Ceremony Held for the Yu-Nan Section; More Than 300 Representatives from All Sectors Attended; After the Meeting, a Visit to the Recovered Bandit Area 135

The Yu-Ping Railway, jointly planned by the Ministry of Railways and the governments of Zhejiang and Jiangxi provinces, has been fully planned after a long period of preparation and design. It has been decided to build the section from Yushan to Nanchang first. The groundbreaking ceremony was held in Yushan at 9:00 AM today (the 8th). Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Zhejiang Construction Department, Zhao Guantao, Commander of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi-Fujian-Anhui Border Region Garrison, Zheng Hua, representative of the Ministry of Railways, and more than 300 representatives from the governments of Zhejiang and Jiangxi provinces and Shanghai Xinkai Community attended. The ceremony was presided over by Zeng Yangfu. In the afternoon, Commander Zhao Guantao hosted various sectors to visit the recovered bandit area in Shangrao, returning to Yushan at about 8:00 PM. At 9:00 PM, a special train returned to Hangzhou. The details are recorded as follows: ▲Ceremony Order: The groundbreaking ceremony was held at 9:00 AM, with the following order: (1) All stand in solemnity; (2) Bow three times to the party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the founding father Dr. Sun Yat-sen; (3) The chairman respectfully reads Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will; (4) Silent tribute; (5) The chairman delivers a speech; (6) The director reports; (7) The commander gives instructions; (8) Guest speeches; (9) Groundbreaking; (10) Photography.

▲Ceremony Site Arrangement: The venue was set up at the end point of the Hangzhou-Yushan section, with a temporary thatched shed built, decorated with green pine trees and flowers, which was quite magnificent. A horizontal banner was hung at the entrance of the venue (Groundbreaking Ceremony for the Yu-Nan Section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway), with a pair of couplets on the left and right, which read (Thousands of miles begin with one step, leveling mountains and determining rivers, opening up wastelands; a line connects Zhejiang and Jiangxi, galloping with the speed of wind and electricity, all things shine together). In the center was the chairman's stage, with seats for news reporters below. A horizontal white cloth banner was hung above (The Great Way is Public), and a couplet was also hung on the left and right, which read (Start operating bravely and forge ahead; rely on the vehicles to assist each other and promote the same customs).

▲Attendees: The attendees included Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Zhejiang Construction Department and Chairman of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Council; Zheng Hua, representative of the Ministry of Railways; Yang Jinzhong, representative of the Zhejiang Provincial Government; Lu Xian, Director of the Civil Affairs Department and representative of the Jiangxi Provincial Government; Li Chukuang, representative of the Zhejiang Provincial Party Department; Yu Baiqing, representative of the Jiangxi Provincial Party Department; Wu Jiantao, Director of the Jiangxi Finance Department and Director of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Council; Xiao Chunjin, member of the Jiangxi Provincial Government and Director of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Council; Guo Su, Administrative Inspector of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi-Fujian-Anhui Border Region; Huo Baoshu, representative of the Bank of China in Shanghai; Shou Yicheng, representative of the Bank of China of the Hangzhou Chamber of Commerce; Hou Jiayuan, Deputy Director of the Nanjing-Jiangxi Railway Bureau; and more than 300 people, including representatives from newspapers in Shanghai and Hangzhou.

▲Chairman's Speech: After the meeting began according to the agenda, Chairman Zeng Yangfu delivered a speech, saying that today is the groundbreaking ceremony for the Yu-Nan section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, and he is very grateful to the leaders and groups for coming in the heat. The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway is a company in name and organization, but its nature is owned by the government, which should be noted. Railways are important transportation undertakings, and Dr. Sun Yat-sen emphasized them in his nation-building strategy. However, Chinese people have always considered railway construction to be extremely difficult, believing that it cannot be operated without foreigners. Since the opening of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway, this kind of fear of difficulty has been swept away. From a technical point of view, some people also doubt that Chinese railways will inevitably lose money and dare not invest. However, if management is proper, there is no reason to lose money. Seeing the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway, the doubts can be dispelled. The Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway's business is based on commercial principles, eliminating all waste and uneconomical expenditures, and for employees, talent is used as the standard, giving them real protection, so that they can work with peace of mind. This is the spirit of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway in the past and present. The mission of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway is even more important. After the devastation of Jiangxi Province by the communist bandits, the restoration of the local economy cannot be achieved without the completion of this road. As for national defense and transportation, it goes without saying. I hope the government and the people will support it.

▲Director's Report: Next, Deputy Director Hou Jiayuan gave a report, saying that the groundbreaking ceremony for this road has been held three times. The first time was in Xiaoshan in 1930, with the purpose of making Xixing directly reach Lanxi. The second time was in Lanxi in 1932, with the purpose of extending from Jinhua to Yushan. Today is the third time, with the purpose of extending this road to Nanchang. At that time, because of the difficulty in raising funds, I never thought that it could become an important railway connecting Zhejiang and Jiangxi provinces. Since the preparations for this road began in May, it has been divided into sixteen sections, of which twelve have been surveyed. The remaining four sections need to wait for one or two weeks after the communist bandits have been wiped out before they can start. The total length of this road is more than 300 kilometers, with a cost of 16 million yuan. It is expected to be completed by the end of next year.

▲Railway Chief's Instructions: Next, Zheng Hua, the representative of the Ministry of Railways, delivered instructions on behalf of Minister Gu, saying that today is the groundbreaking ceremony for the Yu-Nan section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway. Minister Gu of the Ministry of Railways, due to official duties, sent Zheng Hua to participate in the ceremony as a representative. Now, I will follow the instructions of the minister and briefly reiterate the significance and expectations of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway. In the past, the trend of railway construction in our country focused on the north of the Yangtze River, and the vertical and horizontal trunk lines have now been roughly prepared. In the south of the Yangtze River, the Yuehan Railway is the only important trunk line connecting north and south. Now we are rushing to repair the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section, and it is expected to complete the entire line and open it to traffic by 1936. As for the southeastern trunk line, it was originally planned to build the Ningxiang Line, but it could not be realized due to other reasons. Recently, it was decided to use the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway and extend it to become the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, connecting Zhejiang and Jiangxi, reaching Hunan and Anhui, and becoming one of the east-west trunk lines. In the future, after the entire road is completed, it will have great relations with military, political, cultural, and economic aspects, and its position in transportation, connecting to the Yuehan Railway in the west and the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway in the east, is no less than a central communication line. The importance can be imagined. Although the construction of the Yu-Nan section is being carried out first due to limited financial resources, it is hoped that the engineering, management, and accounting systems will be handled in accordance with the standards and regulations set by the Ministry to achieve consistency. At the same time, there are also expectations: 1. For the completed lines of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, the bridges, steel rails, etc. that are not suitable for joint transportation are urgently hoped to be gradually reformed to make their carrying capacity equal to the state-owned railways connected, so that it will be convenient for joint transportation in the future. 2. For the section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway from Nanchang to the west, it is hoped that the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Company will find a way to raise the required construction funds as soon as possible in accordance with the original capital amount, so that it can continue when the Yu-Nan section is completed, and the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section of the Yuehan Railway can be completed and opened to traffic at the same time. The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Company is a unique organization created in response to the central government, local governments, and the financial community, with the Council as the highest executive body. The Council Chairman and others are working hard to build and are specialized talents. It can be foreseen that they will work together with one heart and each show their strengths to establish excellent achievements, which can be congratulated in advance. On the occasion of the groundbreaking, I respectfully deliver my speech. Finally, Wu Jiantao, Yu Baiqing, Xiao Chunjin, Li Chukuang, Zhao Guantao, Huo Baoshu, and others spoke in succession, and the meeting adjourned at 12:00 for photography.

▲Visit to the Bandit Area: At about 1:00 PM, Zhao Guantao, Commander of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi-Fujian-Anhui Border Region Garrison, in order to allow all sectors to understand the situation in the recovered bandit area, specifically invited Zeng Yangfu, Huo Baoshu, Li Chukuang, news reporters from Shanghai and Hangzhou, and guests from all sectors to visit Shangrao and Luoqiao. At 1:30 PM, they set off from Yushan by highway car, arriving at Shangrao City at about 30 minutes. They transferred to Luoqiao. Blockhouses were set up along the road, guarded by the People's Defense Corps organized by residents. According to Commander Zhao, Luoqiao is only 80 li from the communist bandit area, but it has been quite quiet recently. Since the central government adopted a strategy of encirclement and suppression, the communist bandits have been increasingly impoverished and unable to counterattack outwards. It is estimated that after twelve months, the communist bandits in Jiangxi can be completely wiped out. At more than 5:00 PM, the commander hosted a banquet at the Garrison Command in Shangrao City, and the guests and hosts parted happily until 7:00 PM. (Shen Shi News)

Anhui Compatriots Telegraph Request to Avoid Dividing Wuyuan to be Subordinate to Jiangxi 136

And telegraph to compatriots associations in various places to strive for a consistent effort

The Anhui Shanghai Compatriots Association telegraphed the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Central Political Committee, the Ministry of Interior, the Military Committee, Commander-in-Chief Jiang of the Nanchang Forward Headquarters, and the Anhui Provincial Government yesterday regarding the Wuyuan issue, stating:

The Administrative Regions Cannot Be Easily Changed 137

I humbly believe that the establishment and alteration of administrative regions must first thoroughly consider all aspects of the area's history, geography, culture, and economy, taking the convenience of the people and the benefit of governance as the criteria. It cannot be compared to the military zoning, which is about sizing up the terrain to respond to a temporary situation. Furthermore, the boundaries of the two should not be subject to a single administration. Military actions are temporary, administrative measures are permanent, and military authority is directly under the central government. The deployment of troops, the transfer of supplies, and the planning of defense are not restricted by administrative regions.

The Historical and Long-Standing Sentiments of the People of Huizhou 138

Since the proposal to transfer Wuyuan to Jiangxi arose, the people of Huizhou and the villagers of the county have been running around in a panic, telling each other the news. Indeed, for Wuyuan County, historically, all counties under Huizhou have been under the same administration for more than a thousand years; geographically, they are all mountainous areas belonging to the Huangshan mountain range; culturally, they are all influenced by the theories of Zhu Xi, Tao Xingzhi, Jiang Yong, and Dai Zhen; economically, the land is barren, agriculture is underdeveloped, and most people are engaged in long-distance trade. Their customs are similar, and their feelings are deep. Therefore, the fellow townsmen of Huizhou in various ports regard each other as siblings. If the county is transferred to Jiangxi, separating it from other counties under Huizhou and placing it under the same administrative organization as Dexing, Fuliang, and Leping counties, where the customs of farming on plains are robust, it will not only cause great inconvenience in life, but also political measures will likely be incompatible.

The Military Operations to Suppress Bandits Should Be Unified Early 139

If some argue that it is necessary for the convenience of suppressing bandits, then the troops suppressing bandits from the three provinces and the local police are all under the command of Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of our Military Affairs Commission. The troops currently stationed in Wuyuan are subordinates of the Commander-in-Chief of the Reserve Army and do not have the boundaries of Anhui and Jiangxi to begin with. Why is it necessary to change the jurisdiction in order to take advantage of the terrain and ensure a perfect defense?

The Principle of the Premier's Political Power Emphasizes Public Opinion 140

In the past, our Premier separated political power and governing power, with the former belonging to the people and the latter belonging to the government. Although we have not yet reached the constitutional era, the direction of public opinion should be sufficient for the government to consider. Therefore, based on this principle, we make a straightforward appeal, hoping that the ministries and commissions of the government will carefully consider the people's concerns and re-examine this case to benefit the people's livelihood and appease their expectations. Anhui Association in Shanghai kowtows with utmost urgency to await orders. We also send messages to the Anhui associations and prominent figures in Beijing, Hangzhou, Tianjin, Suzhou, Shandong, Henan, Hubei, Guangdong, and Hankou, urging them to strive for this matter together. (Telegram omitted)

The Head of the Local Patrol, Shen Mingming, Has His Appeal Against the Red Pill Trafficking Case Rejected and Will Still be Executed According to the Original Sentence 143

Shen Mingming, a local resident and head of the local patrol residing in a bungalow without a number on Ninghe Road, is 52 years old. Previously, Xu Guiying, a detective from the Narcotics Division, learned that he was selling red pills for profit. He sent an informant to buy them, each time for 20 cents, for a total of three times, amounting to three small packets. At noon on May 25th, he and the western patrol leader, Pat Pu, went to the address and arrested Shen. They also found four medium-sized packets of red pills in a bamboo basket under the eaves of the house. They were all taken to the Yangshupu Police Station and sent to the First Special District Local Court, where Shen Mingming was sentenced to two years of imprisonment and fined 1,000 yuan.

Shen refused to accept the sentence and hired lawyer Zhang to appeal to the Second Branch of the High Court. After deliberation, a date was set for the pronouncement of the verdict. Yesterday, Judge Zhao Cheng personally presided over the First Criminal Court and ruled that Shen Mingming's appeal was rejected and that the original sentence would be executed.

The Verdict in the Welfare Company Theft Case: Li Zhenhua and Others Are Sentenced Separately 144

Li Zhenhua, a shop assistant at the Welfare Company on Nanjing Road, colluded with Wang Atao, who had left the store, Li Linggen, and Luo Yingquan, the gatekeeper, to steal a large number of silk stockings, ties, blankets, and clothing worth more than a thousand yuan. Later, Li was caught selling stolen goods at the Tianyunlou Amusement Park. Shen Jinwen and Pang Ruiqing, detectives from the Laozha Police Station, arrested Li and found a large amount of stolen goods worth more than a thousand yuan at Li's house at No. 120 Oujia Road. They also arrested Luo, Wang, and Li. The police lawyer, Gan Jingxian, prosecuted them in the First Special Court under Article 338 of the Criminal Law. After the interrogation was completed, Judge Qian Hongye announced the verdict yesterday, sentencing Li Zhenhua to one year and six months of imprisonment, and Wang Atao, Li Linggen, and Luo Yingquan to one year of imprisonment each. The stolen goods were returned to the plaintiff.

Not only is the autumn harvest hopeless, but people and animals are also suffering. Such an unprecedented catastrophe is deeply pitiful. Each public office will continue for another three days. After the Gongo Lun Ship Lost Caution and Was Extinguished, the Joint Inspection Surveyed the Burned Goods; The Cause of the Fire Was Self-Combustion Due to Hot Weather; The Loss Was 10,000 Yuan, and the Ship Will Sail to Wuhan as Usual Tonight 159

The British Yihua Company's Shanghai-Wuhan route Gongo Lun ship lost caution. After being extinguished by the Jianghai Customs fire boat, an investigation was conducted yesterday morning, and the loss was 10,000 yuan. The ship will sail to Hankou as usual tonight. The details are recorded as follows.

Extinguishing the Import 160

After the Gongo Lun ship lost caution and docked outside Wusongkou, the Jianghai Customs sent two fireboats and cooperated with the Shanghai Public Concession Fire Brigade for rescue. It was not completely extinguished until about 3 p.m. the day before yesterday. At 10 p.m. the night before, it entered Wusongkou and originally docked at the Hongkou Shuntai Wharf. Yihua Company immediately notified the cargo owner, Shen Heng Foreign Firm at 190 Jiujiang Road.

Inspection Survey Yesterday Morning 161

At 10 a.m. yesterday morning, the British Yihua Company sent personnel to the Huashun Wharf together with the cargo owner, Shen Heng Foreign Firm, and the Insurance Association for inspection. The waste cotton loaded in the fourth cargo hold was burned by the fire, and the rest was waterlogged. However, the other cargo holds were not affected, and the ship's hull was not damaged. After the inspection, a report was made and filed for future reference, so as to claim compensation from the company insuring against water and fire risks.

Starting to Unload Cargo 162

The cargo loaded in the fourth cargo ship was waste cotton, totaling 1,226 pieces, all of which belonged to Shen Heng Foreign Firm. After being burned, Shen Heng Foreign Firm hired barges yesterday afternoon to unload the waterlogged waste cotton and transport it to the Longmao Wharf warehouse in Pudong for temporary storage. Because the insurance policy of the insurance company has not yet been sent from Hankou to Shanghai, it was telegraphed to Hankou yesterday morning to inquire which company insured the goods and to send the insurance policy to Shanghai as soon as possible for settlement.

Cause of the Fire 163

Reporters from Xin Sheng News Agency learned from Yihua Company and Shen Heng Foreign Firm that the more than 1,200 pieces of waste cotton loaded in the fourth cargo hold were mostly oil cotton in the waste cotton, which is easy to catch fire. The fire started at 3 p.m. on July 7th and was not extinguished until 4 p.m. on July 8th, a total of 26 hours. The reason was that the weather was hot, and the oil cotton self-combusted due to accumulation, which was definitely not caused by leaving a cigarette butt behind.

Total Loss 164

According to the news from Shen Heng Foreign Firm, there were 1,226 pieces of waste cotton, each worth about six taels of silver, which is about 10,000 yuan. Most of them have been burned and waterlogged, and they are likely to be useless and will definitely be completely lost. As for the Gongo Lun ship, it was not damaged at all. After the cargo is unloaded, it will be scheduled to sail from Shanghai to Wuhan as usual at 12 p.m. tomorrow night, stopping at all ports.

Zhang Awei, One of the "Four Great Kings" of Flower Gambling, Was Arrested; A Large Number of Flower Gambling Tickets and Gambling Funds Were Seized; Zhang Has Been Sent to the Third Section of the General Bureau for Interrogation 165

Although the police and detectives have repeatedly cracked down on and arrested people involved in flower gambling dens in the Zhabei area, those who are banned are banned, and those who commit offenses continue to do so. Not long after, he returned to his old ways, setting up four flower gambling listening posts and sending people to collect gambling funds and flower gambling deposit tickets from Zhabei and the South City every day. Gamblers flocked to him.
